1623

Co-operative Societies Ordinance, 1984

 

 

Co-operative Societies Ordinance, 1984

Section- 19(2) And

Constitution of Bangladesh, 1972

Articles-27 and 38

 

(a) Section-19(2) of the Co-operative Societies Ordinance challenged by the petitioner who was elected for 3 consecutive terms, a member of the Managing Committee of a Co-operative Society is not violative of the Articles-27 and 38 of the Bangladesh Constitution though S. 19(2) imposes restriction on a citizen rendering the petitioner uneligible for being elected as an officer of the Co-operative Society unless a period of 2 years elapsed before the expiry of his last term as a member of the said society—the petitioner was not treated unequally. [Para-5]

Md. Abdus Sattar Vs. Bangladesh 1 BLT (AD)-31                                                                                                                                                       

(b) Interpretation of the legislative intent-old is gold- “the old order changeth yielding place to new-reasonableness of restriction.

“While the proverb “old is gold” has a fatal attraction, another proverb “the old order changeth yielding place to new” is equally honoured. Which proverb to following what given situation is a legislative exercise and it cannot be said that barring a thrice-elected Member of the Managing Committee to stand for election again till the lapse of 2 years since his last term expired is an unreasonable restriction.” [Para-5]

Md. Abdus Sattar Vs. Bangladesh 1 BLT(AD)-31

1624

Code of Civil Procedure, 1908 (Order XII - XLVII)

Citation: 7 BLT (AD)-153, 7 BLT (HCD)-296,7 BLT (HCD)-355, 2 BLT (HCD)- 142, 4 BLT (AD)-161, 5 BLT (HCD)-36, 4 BLT (HCD)- 113, 6 BLT (HCD)-22, 7 BLT (HCD)-286, 6 BLT (HCD)-150, 6 BLT (HCD)-88, 5 BLT (HCD)- 140, 1 BLT (AD)-25,6 BLT (HCD)-123, 2 BLT (HCD)-179, 2

Subject: Civil Procedure

Delivery Date: 1970-01-01

 

 

Order-7 Rule-11

From the averments in the plaint, it is found that the suspension order was passed without prior show cause. The plaintiff having been adversely affected by the suspension order has filed the suit and as such it cannot be said that he has no cause of action to file the suit. Further, whether the suit is barred under Section 42 of the Specific Relief Act, or not is a matter which could be mooted as an issue in the suit. Thus it cannot be said that there is no cause of action and the suit is barred by any law. [Para-61

Alhaj B. N. Khan (Degree) College Vs. Md. Abdur Rahim & Ors. 7 BLT (AD)-153.

Order-7 Rule-11

In the instant case, no act of the Corporation has been challenged in the suit by the plaintiffs. The plaintiffs prayed for declaration that they are entitled to get the suit lands derequisitioned in their favour and also for a decree of khas possession— Held: Since no act of the Corporation has been challenged by the plaintiffs in the suit, they were not required to serve any notice as contemplated under Section 74 of the Ordinance of 1961 and the plaint also cannot be rejected for non-service of notice under the said section of the said Ordinance. [Para-26J

BADC Vs. Abedunnessa & Ors. 7 BLT (HCD)-296.

Order-7 Rule-11

Question of maintainability—In the present suit the Chairman is representing the Corporation as the chief functionary and as such the objection that instead of the Corporation itself, the Chairman is made defendant in the suit is a technical objection. It is posited here that the contention raised is a question of maintainability which does not come within the four walls of the provisions of Order-Vu, Rule-il of the Code and this question of maintainability can be agitated by the defendant-petitioner at the time of hearing of the suit. [Para-31]

BADC Vs. Abeduanessa & Ors. 7 BLT (HCD)-296.

Order-7 Rule-11

Question of res-judicata— In the present case, there is nothing to show from the averments as made in the plaint, the suit appears to be barred by law. However if the observations as made by the Special Bench of the High Court Division to the effect that the suit is barred by principles of res-judicata reached its finality, then however the petitioners could argue that the aforesaid view should be read along with the plaint but since a civil appeal has been filed against the above orders on dated 10.3.97 and 19.6.97 of the Special Bench passed in F.M.A. No. 81 of 1996 and the same is pending for hearing in the Appellate Division, at the (the) aforesaid view of the Special Bench of the High Court Division cannot be read along with the plaint of the present suit. However when the suit may be taken up for hearing defendants will be at liberty to raise this issue of res judicata relying on the judgments passed in Writ Petition No. 3734 of 1992 along with observations made in F.M.A. No. 81 of 1996 and under the provision of Order 14 Rule 2 C.P.C. the learned Subordinate Judge may be postponing other issues of fact, hear this issue of law regarding maintainability of the suit on the principles of res-judicata.

Chairman, RMUK Vs. Md. Jobed Ali & Ors 7 BLT (HCD)-355.

Order-7 Rule-11

The opposite party No.1 being plaintiff instituted the other classes suit before the Subordinate Judge challenging the order of termination of service being void, illegal, inoperative, ultra-vires and has no binding effect upon him and also for a declaration that the plaintiffs service as driver as Sonali Bank was still continuing with all salaries and benefits — the defendants No. 4 and 6 and 6 appeared and filed an application, praying for rejecting the plaint on the ground that no ad valorem court fee was paid and that the forum for challenging such order of termination of service was the Labour court and not the ordinary civil court — the learned Sub-Judge rejected the said application as the defendants petitioners finding that the ad valorem court fee is not necessary in a suit like this and since the order of termination was challenged in the suit, it is not barred under any law before the Civil Court — the Civil Court had got the jurisdiction to entertain such a suit challenging the order of termination in as much as the plaintiff being worker had no other forum to challenge this order of termination from service that termination of service was not challenged on the ground of any trade union activities of the plaintiff worker — the learned Sub-Judge in deciding this matter has not committed any error and hence this Rule is discharged. [Paras-2 & 9]

Sonali Bank & Ors Vs. Md. Abul Khaiyar & Ors 2 BLT (HCD)- 142.

Order-7 Rule-11

“Equity and good conscious”—The plaintiff instituted the Title Suit Praying for a decree for mandatory injunction directing the defendants to send his minor son to his residence in terms of the agreement entered into by and between the plaintiff and defendant No. 1—defendants filed an application under Order 7 Rule 11 of the C.P.C for rejection of the plaints on the ground that the suit should have been filed before the Family Court, as the Civil Court had no jurisdiction to try the suit—Held The phrase “equity and good conscious” are not in Order 7 Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure and as such the learned Single Judge wrongly imported this concept in the section which he was not permitted to do— appeal in allowed. [Para- 11]

M. I. Sayed Vs. M. R. Matin & Ors. 4 BLT (AD)-161.

Order-7 Rule-11

Whether the plaint should be rejected - The court can reject the plaint only when it comes to the conclusion that even if all the allegations made in the plaint are proved still then the plaintiffs would not be entitled to any relief whatsoever. [Para-7]

Most. Nurunnessa Vs. Mahibuddin Chowdhury 5 BLT (HCD)-36.

Order-7 Rule- 11(d) Read with Order-8 Rule -6

The opposite parties made a counter claim against the plaintiff petitioner on different counts as damages and compensation—the plaintiff-petitioner filed an application in the trial court for rejecting the prayer of counter claim. The said application was rejected by the trial court holding that the counter claim was made under the relevant provisions of the Code of Civil Procedure which is applicable in the proceedings of Artha Rin Adalat—Held: we have examined the provisions of the Act and there is no Provision for making counter claim by a defendant—Even if it were held that the Civil Procedure Code is applicable in the instant case then also the trial court acted illegally and without jurisdiction in as much as the counter claim raised by the defendant do not come within the perview of Rule-6 of Order 8 as the sum claimed by way of damage is not an ascertained amount. [Paras- 15 & 16]

Sonali Bank Vs. M/S Ali Tannery Ltd. & Ors 4 BLT (HCD)-  113.

Order-8 Rule-5

Order 8 Rule 5 of the Code of Civil Procedure provides that assertion of facts made in the plaint if not denied specifically or by necessary implication, shall be deemed to be admitted. In our case under review the plaintiff clearly stated in the plaint that Lakshman Mondal had died in this country as a citizen of the erstwhile East Pakistan leaving the plaintiff as his only heir to succeed him and he led evidence to prove the said assertion by the unchallenged oral and documentary evidence and there being no contrary evidence on record, the learned Courts below clearly erred in law in dismissing the suit ignoring the positive evidence on record by resorting to hypothetical assumptions and the same has resulted in error in the impugned decision occasioning failure of justice. [Para- 16]

Maran Mondal & Ors. Vs. A. D. C. (Rev). 6 BLT (HCD)-22.

Order-8 Rule-6

Application for transposition of the defendant as plaintiff—the vessel was arrested by Bombay High Court and in the scisin of the matter in dispute being Admiralty Suit No. 44. It appears further that admittedly there are series of transaction in between the parties at different places and countries starting from Rangoon and ultimately the vessel was arrested when it was discharging business at Haldia in India by order of the Court. In such circumstances where the plaintiff withdraw the suit, the prayer of the defendant to proceed with the counter claim treating it as plaint is not maintainable. [Para-1 1]

Loyal Shipping Ltd. Vs. Custom U. K. Ltd. 7 BLT (HCD)-286.

Order-9 Rule-3

In the instant case, on the relevant date, the plaintiff was not absent from the court, but he made an application praying for issuance of warrant of arrest against the defendant No. 3 for the purpose of examination and comparison by a finger print expert with the disputed signature. Therefore, after rejecting the application for issuance of warrant without passing further order directing the parties to get ready passing of the order of dismissal of the suit is hit by Order 9 Rule 3 of the Civil Procedure Code. It is held that a suit cannot be dismissed Order 9 Rule 3 of the Code. When the plaintiff made an application in the court as referred above treating the posijon as absence of the plaintiff, which is apparently illegal. [Para-9]

Md. Nojatullah Vs. Alokeshi Namasudra & Ors. 6 BLT (HCD)-150.

Order-9 Rule-4

Mandatory provisions—in the instant case petitioner of Misc. Case No. 71 of 1984 did not examine any witness in support of his case. Except his uncorroborated statements incorporated in his application under Order 9 Rule 4 of the Code of Civil Procedure there is absolutely nothing on record to prove that he was prevented by any sufficient cause from appearing before the Couft when the case was called for hearing and this led to the dismissal of his case for default. In the absence of any evidence before him providing necessary satisfaction that the petitioner was really prevented by sufficient cause from appearing before the Court on the fateful day, the learned trial Court clearly erred in law in allowing Miscellaneous Case No. 71 of 1984 completely ignoring the mandatory provisions of Order 9 Rule 4 of the Code of Civil Procedure. [Para-9]

Harendra Nath Mandal Vs. Chitta Ranjan Halder & Ors 6 BLT (HCD)-88.

Order-9 Rule-4

After the restoration of a suit at the instance of the plaintiff, the defendants become entitled both in equity and as of right to notice of the date fixed for hearing of the suit after its restoration on setting aside of the order of dismissal for default relied on AIR 1933 ALL, 522 and AIR 1945, Nagpur, 185. (Para-10)

Md. Siddique Vs. Teakuti Begum & Ors. 5 BLT (HCD)- 140

Order-9 Rule-6( 1)(a)

The Latin expression “ex parte” meaning not defined in the Code of Civil Procedure— basic principles of adversary procedure followed in court system—exception to the principle—procedure under Order-9, Rule6(1) C.P.C.—no mandate as to passing an ex parte decree in C.P.C.

‘The Latin expression ‘ex parte’ meaning from one party or side, has not been defined in the Code of Civil Procedure. One of the basic principles of the adversary procedure followed in our court system is that as far as possible. No proceeding be conducted to the detriment of a person in his absence. One exception to this principle is that when the defendant, duly served with summons, does not avail himself of the opportunity to appear, the court may proceed in his absence under Rule-6(1)(a) of Order-IX. There being no mandate as such to make ex parte’ decree the court may order for fresh service of summons on the defendants or adjourn the matter suo motu. If the court is satisfied that the summons was duly served on the defendant may proceed to decide the matter. [Para- 11]

Alfu Miah and others Vs. Bangladesh 1 BLT (AD)-25.

There is no hard and fast rule for writing an ex parte judgment

‘These observations made with regard to a suit filed under the Code of Civil Procedure it was held in Mst. Nurjahan Begum V. Giri Gopal Sarker 1979 BSCR (VI. 3) 400 (402), would in substance apply in a case under the Small Causes Courts Act. 1887. It was further observed that ‘the trial court must set out the point for determination and the reason for determination and this will again be arrived at on evidence on record and the evidence on record must establish the case of the plaintiff which again must show a cause of action. It is true that there Is no hard and fast rule for writing an ex parte judgment. If the substance of what has been set out herein are complied with the ex parte judgment, however brief in expression, will stand. It will be difficult to sustain an ex parte judgment which does not satisfy the condition of law as set out earlier.” [Para-7]

Alfu Miah and Others Vs. Bangladesh 1 BLT (AD)-25.

Passing of an ex-parte decree—court’s duty

“Before an ex-parte decree is passed the court is required to go through the records whether such a decree could be passed on the assertions/evidence of the plaintiff, but the court is not required to delve deep into the matter and ferret out a defence plea that may lead to the dismissal of the plaintiffs case.” [Para- 12]

Alfu Miah and Others Vs. Bangladesh 1 BLT (AD)-25.

Order-9 Rule-13

It appears from Order No. 15 dated 11.8.86 that the summons was not as yet served upon defendant No. 2, who is the petitioner before me and 20.8.86 was fixed for service summons upon him. It is crystal clear from this order dated 11.8.86 that defendant No. 2 was surreptitiously made defendant No. 3 subsequently by an unscrupulous zealot by interpolation which is easily discernible from a cursory look at the order sheet and this fact is further magnified by Order No. 16 dated 28.8.86 wherein it was specifically mentioned that the next date of the suit was fixed on 11.9.86 for service return of summons upon defendant No. 2 by usual process as well as by registered post. After that there is no order in the entire order sheet indicating that summons was ever served upon defendant No. 2 in the usual course. There is also no clear proof on record to find that summons by registered post was duly served upon defendant No. 2. Although by order No. 33 dated 24.5.87 the trial Court in a casual manner found that notice upon defendant No. 2 was served by registered post under the provisions of Section 19(b) sub-clause (2) of the Code of Civil Procedure but except this stray observation made in the order sheet there is no other material on record, to prove that summons was duly served upon defendant No. 2 either by the usual process or by registered post. From this it is manifestly clear that no summons was served upon defendant No. 2 as required by law—Held: In the instant case, since there was no due service of summons upon defendant No. 2 (petitioner) impugned decree is liable to be set aside. [Paras-5 & 9]

Md. Yousuf Ali Vs. Araj Ali & Ors 6 BLT (HCD)-123.

Order-9 Rule-13

The report of summons of the peon of the court it appears that showing defendants No. 2 as minor notice has been served upon his elder brother defendant No. 1 and in that report of peon of the court it has been mentioned that defendant No. 1 refused to take notice (summon) of the court and as such it has been served by hanging notice on door of the house of the defendant No. 1. No notice was served upon the defendants directly and as such the serving of notice upon the defendants become doubtful and in such a case the ex-parte decree will be set aside even if the defendant had knowledge of the institution of the suit. [Para- 13]

Md. Abul Hossain & Ors Vs. Nironjan Mondal & Ors 2 BLT (HCD)-179.

Order-9 RuIe-13 Read with Section-151

The ex parte decree was passed on the first date of hearing of the suit after receipt of the summons, that the application under Order 9. Rule 13 of C.P.C was made on the very next day of the passing of the ex parte decree and the restoration of the suit was made on payment of adequate cost—appeal is allowed. [Paras - 9 & 10]

Mohon Bashi Nama Vs Golam Rashid & Ors 2 BLT (AD)-162.

Sufficient cause for the long delay in filing an application under Order-9 Rule-13

The suit was decreed on ex parte on 24.12.79 against opposite party. An appeal was pending before the Additional Deputy Commissioner (Rev) amongst the parties that the said appear was fixed for hearing on 20.5.81 when it was disclosed that the petitioners got the suit land by the ex parte decree from the Civil Court and on this way the opposite party No. 1 come to know about the ex parte decree that after search finally come to learn on 30.5.1981 about the ex parte decree at Civil Court through their engaged lawyer—the defendants gave sufficient explanation about the delay in filing the Miscellaneous Case as they had no earlier knowledge about the filing of the suit and they could come to know about the ex parte decree only on 20.5. 1981. [Paras-3. 4 & 14]

Md. Abul Hossain & Ors Vs. Nironjan Mondal & Ors. 2 BLT (HCD)-179.

Order-9 Rule-13

Decree passed in a suit ex parte — there were two defendants — the process server reported that he went to the defendant’s residence and when the husband of defendant No. 1 refused to accept the summons it was served by hanging. The process server is silent on mode of service of summons or attempt to service of summons on defendant No. 2—attesting witness stated that the process server in his presence served the summons on defendant No. 2. He has not stated a single word on the service of summons on defendant No. 1—who dictated each other on the service of summons—actually there was sending of the summons by registered post with A/D. There is nothing on record to Indicate that the postal A/D was received by the trial court and no step was taken in the case by the respondent to examine the postal peon to prove the service of summons sent by registered post with A/D the process server, report on the service of summons which cannot be construed and accepted as proper and legal service of summons and the provisions of Rule 19 B of Order 5 of the C.P.C has not been complied with — a fraud has been committed upon the court as well as upon the appellant by the plaintiff of the original suit in getting the ex parte decree and as such restore the original suit to its file and number. [Paras- 11, 12 & 20]

Mathura Mohan Pandit Vs Most. Hazera Khatun 2 BLT (HCD)-215.

Order-9 Rule-13

In an application under order 9, rule- 13 of the Code of Civil Procedure praying for setting aside the ex parte decree the whole onus is upon the plaintiff to prove that summons was duly served upon the defendant. [Para- 10]

Md. Wazed Ali Sardar Vs. Md. Afsaruddin Sardar and Ors. 4 BLT (AD) 1.

Order-9 Rule-13

Clerks’ failure to inform his advocate of the date of hearing will not be regarded as a sufficient ground for his nonappearance—exceptions to this rule stated.

“A Counsel is responsible for representing his client’s case ordinarily his clerk’s failure to inform him about the date of hearing of case will not be regarded as a sufficient ground for his non-appearance. There may, however, be special circumstances indicating the learned counsel’s total dependence on his clerk because of his illness or such other good reason when a clerk’s failure to inform the date of hearing to the counsel may amount to be a sufficient cause for the counsel’s non-appearance at the time of the hearing. No special case has been made out in this case. [Para-15]

Alfu Miah and others Vs. Bangladesh 1 BLT (AD)-25. 

Order-9 Rule- 13

General Principle - A person cannot and/or ought not to be permitted to approbate and reprobate at the same time, the respondents were not entitled to question the order of restoration of the suit after having accepted the cost which was made a condition for the restoration. [Para-9]

Mohan Bashi Nama Vs. Golam Rashid & Ors. 2 BLT (AD)-162.

Order-11 Rule-15

Under Rule 15 Court may pass an order debarring the defaulting party from putting into evidence the documents which were not produced in Court in compliance of the notice served upon him by his adversary. Para-5

Abdul Jalil & Ors. Vs. Hossainia Trust 4 BLT (AD)-226.=

Order-11 Rule-21

By using the clauses ‘an order may be made accordingly’ the Provision of Rule-21 has, clearly, been made not mandatory, rather a discretion has been given to the Court — if the defendant has failed to produce certain documents and if he is barred from producing those documents, against which he has not moved the higher forum, he will precluded from leading evidence on a part of his written statement, but for that failure, the trial Court obviously found it unnecessary to strike off his entire written statement. [Paras-6 & 7]

Abdul Jalil & Ors. Vs. Hossainia Trust 4 BLT (AD)-226.

Order-11 Rule-21

The provisions of answering interrogatories—in the instant case, the party interrogated has not failed to comply with any order of the court to answer interrogatories the party interrogated has answered the interrogatories within the time granted by the court—the provision of Rule 21 applies when the party interrogated fails to comply with an order passed by the Court under Rule 11, but in the instant case the party interrogated has not failed to comply with any order of the Court. [Para- 161

Bisheswar Bhattacharjee Vs. Santimoy Bhattacharjee & Ors 7 BLT (HCD)-323.

Order-14 Rule-2 & Order- 15 Rule-3 Read with

Code of Civil Procedure (Amendment) Ordinance, 1983, Order-20 Rule-5

It is true that it is within the discretionary power of the trial Judge to hear a preliminary issue but on hearing the preliminary issue he is not authorised to decide and dismiss the suit and he is to postpone the settlement of issues of fact and all the issues are to be decided along with the issue of maintainability can be decided on the completion of evidences and at the time of pronouncement of the judgment. [Para-35]

Aziza Nilufar Begum Vs. Jahanara Begum & Anr 6 BLT (HCD)-56.

Order-14 Rule-1

The trial court, besides the issues framed in the regular course, took up an additional issue for decision; Has the plaintiff acquired any title to the suit land by adverse possession?

Held : Order XIV Rule-i of the Code of Civil Procedure casts a definite responsibility upon the trial court to frame issue upon the material assertions by one party and denied by the other and this can be done at any stage of suit if found necessary provided that the parties are afforded a chance to contest the issue. [Para-81

M. Abdul Jalil Miah Vs. Niropama Richil & Ors. 5 BLT (AD)-91.

 

Order- 14 Rule-1

Framing of issues—wrong issue—non framing of a particular issue is only an irregularity and not illegality and that has not in any way prejudiced the parties when points of issue has been correctly decided— relied on 43 DLR - 170 and 34 DLR - 267. [Para-14]

S. B. Krishna Dey Vs. M. Haque & Ors. 4 BLT (HCD)-118.

Order-14 Rule-2 & Order- 15 Rule -3

Rejecting the prayer for disposal of the issue of law on res-judicata—the plaintiffs filed a suit for permanent injunction against the defendants-petitioners. The suit was dismissed on contest and the appeal preferred against the decree by the plaintiffs was also dismissed, without challenging the appellate decision before higher forum the plaintiffs instituted a suit for declaration and confirmation of possession of the self some properties. The defendants petitioners appeared and confirmation of possession of the self some properties. The defendents-petitioners appeared and filed two petitions alleging the bar of res-judicata—one before filing the written statement and the other on the date of filing of the written statement—both the prayer were rejected. The defendents did not challenge those orders before the higher forum either. The learned Judge by his impugned order rejected the petition on the ground that decision on similar matter had already given on 2.8.88 with a direction upon the parties to get ready for hearing of the suit. This is a clear case of res-judicata and as such the learned Judge ought to have determined this issue of law first as contended by the petitioners’ counsel.

Held : In this revision we are not called upon to decide whether on the materials on record the suit was actually hit by bar of res-judicata; we will see whether the learned Judge exercise his discretion in arbitrary and unreasonable manner in rejecting the defendants prayer for determination of the issue first—making the prayer on the date fixed for final hearing is to frustrate the object of order 14 rule 2 and order 15 rule 3 to avoid protracted litigation and unnecessary expenditure. On this ground alone the learned Judge must be held to have properly exercised his discretion in rejecting the belated prayer—relied on 30 DLR(SC)-30. [Para-8]

Hatem Ali & Ors. Vs. Ranan Ali & Ors. 4 BLT (HCD)-106.

Order-16 Rule-10(1)(3)

A civil court can issue warrant of arrest to ensure appearance of any witness or party in a litigation, before it, if the court thinks his presence necessary for final and effective decision in a dispute. [Para-9]

Md. Nojabatullah Vs. Alokeshi Namasudra & Ors. 6 BLT (RCD)-150.

Order- 18 Rule-17

Application for recalling the P. Ws—the powers under the rule one very wide and court can recall a witness even while considering its judgment if any ambiguity or omission is noticed. The powers can be exercised suo motu and also at the instance of a party —the questions which the petitioner wanted to put to the said P.Ws. after recalling appears to be very much relevant and Parliament for determining the issues involved in the suit— Rule is made absolute—relied on AIR 192 13 (PC) 95. [Paras-7 & 9]

Abdul Wadud Vs. The State 3 BLT (HCD)-258.

Order- 18 Rule- 16 Read with Order-26 Rule-1

Before completion of examination of the P.Ws. the defendants filed an application for examination of one witness on commission that application was allowed after heating both the parties—the Court below has not committed any error of law since the court can exercise its jurisdiction to examine any witness at any stage of the procedure of the Court if so satisfied as provided under Order 18 Rule 16 C.P.C. [Para-6]

K. M. Golam Akber & Ors Vs. Amir Hamja & Ors. 3 BLT (HCD)-27.

Order-20 Rule-1

Plaintiff appellant instituted title suit for specific performance of contract against the defendant respondents—the learned Assistant Judge upon considering the evidence in the case by his judgment and decree dated 25.1.84 decreed the suit on contest against defendant No. 1 with cost an ex parte against the rest without cost — it was also directed that “the plaintiff must deposit the balance consideration price of Tk-3000/- by 15.2.1984 failing which the suit shall stand dismissed”—the plaintiff being unaware of the judgment and order dated 25.11.1984 could not make the deposit in time in spite of having the judgment in his favour — admittedly the judgment in the present case was not delivered after the hearing of the arguments on 12.1.1984 and the date for judgment was fixed on 22.1.1984. In the daily cause list of 22.1.1984 the matter did appear for judgment but evidently the judgment was not delivered as the matter appeared for judgment again in the ‘daily cause list’ of 6.2.1984 — Held The party’s and their lawyers source of information about the suit etc. is the ‘daily cause list’/register of the court. There is nothing on record to show that the plaintiff or his lawyer had otherwise any information or knowledge that the judgment would be delivered on 25.1.1984—in the facts and circumstances of the case we hold that there has been a clear miscarriage of justice by reason of non-consideration either by the learned Subordinate Judge or by the learned Judge of the High Court Division of a simple and apparent fact. The omission is such as cannot be adequately deplored—appeal is allowed. [Paras-15 & 16]

Md. Sumon Miah Vs. Falani Begum & Ors. 3 BLT (AD)-221.

Order-20 Rule 4(1)

No necessity to give elaborate judgment.

‘The court is not required to give an elaborate judgment. How far a judgment passed in an ex parte proceeding is to comply with the provisions of Order-20 Rule4(1) of the Code will depend on facts of each case.” [Para- 13]

Alfu Miah and others Vs. Bangladesh 1 BLT (AD)-25.

Order - 20 Rule - 4

Ex parte—while passing the judgment even ex parte the court is required to comply with the provisions of order 20, rule-4, C.P.C. which prescribes that the judgment of the courts shall contain a concise statement of the case, the points for determination, the decision thereon and the reasons for such decisions—relied on 25 DLR (AD) 90, 1 BLD (AD) 371 & 45 DLR (AD) 112. [Para-7]

Samarendra Nath Ghoswami Vs. Helena Herlovi & Ors 4 BLT (HCD)-163.

Speed in which the suit should be disposed of

There is no doubt that every suit should be decided as quickly as possible but justice should not only be done, but should manifestly and undoubtedly be seem to be done. [Para -8]

Samarendra Nath Ghoswami Vs. Helena Herlovi & Ors 4 BLT (HCD)-163.

Order-20 Rule 4(2) and Rule-5

Passing of an ex parte decree — in the impugned ex parte judgment and decree, has not uttered a single word in respect of possession of the parties in the suit land though it is a suit for permanent injunction wherein question of possession is of vital importance and also about the documents, not legally proved and marked as exhibits— the minimum legal requirements in passing the ex parte judgment and decree have not been complied with—the impugned ex-parte judgment and decree cannot be sustained in law—Rule absolute. [Para-5]

Priyabala Debi & Others Vs Babul Chakrabarty 2 BLT (HCD)-48.

Order-21 Rule-29

Admittedly both the Sec. Suits are not in the same court and Order 21 Rule 29 of the Code has got no manner of application in this case when the proceedings was stayed are not pending in the same court. [Para-9]

Monowara Begum Vs. Atiqullah 7 BLT (HCD)-193.

Order-21 Rule-32

Objectionable remarks—Age of the petitioner is of no relevance

The learned Assistant Judge taking a correct view of law and facts and on proper scrutiny of materials and evidence on record rightly passed the impugned order. Since by the impugned order the petitioner No. 1 has been sentenced to undergo civil imprisonment for 15 days the age of the petitioner No. 1 is of no relevance. In that view of the matter I am of the view that in the instant case no lenient view can be taken simply on the ground that the petitioner No. 1 is aged about 60 years and fact remains that he has violated the courts order and ousted the plaintiff opposite party from the suit land. [Para-8]

Madhu & Ors Vs. Maharam Ali 7 BLT (HCD)-358.

Order-21 Rule-38

The maintainability of the second application under Order 21 Rule 38 C.P.C. was challenged on the ground that It was barred by resjudicata, an earlier application having been dismissed by the Artha Rin Adalat. The High Court Division rightly held that the principle of resjudicata is not applicable in such proceeding. [Para-91

Sonali Bank Vs. S. Razia Nahar & Ors 4 BLT (AD)-155.

Order-21 Rule-77(2)

Public auction of moveable property — In the instant case the auction sale was held on 5.11.88 and the executing court accepted the quotation of the auction purchaser appellant the auction sale of the appellant was formally accepted by the court by its order dated 10.11.88 giving time to the auction purchaser appellant to deposit the entire deed amount by 15.11.88 and the same was duly deposited — sale become absolute and cannot be set aside. [Para- 12]

Fariduddin Chowdhury Vs. M/S Sylhet Glass Works Ltd & Ors 3 BLT (AD)-168.

Order-22 Rule-3

The Code of Civil Procedure does not prescribe any special ‘Form” for making such application for substitution. But as a matter of practice such application is made furnishing the legal requirements viz, the date of death of the deceased, names and other particulars of his heirs to be substituted and their relationship with the deceased and as to whether such application has been made within the prescribed period of limitation. [Para- 10]

Md. Siddique Rahman & Ors. Vs. Profulla Bala Devi & Ors 6 BLT (AD)-57.

Order-22 Rule-4 (4)

Five Miscellaneous cases were filed under section 96 for pre-emption. During pendency of these cases opposite party No. 2, 13 & 22 died leaving behind heirs. The petitioners of all these cases filed petitions for striking out the name of the deceased opposite parties — the trial court rejected the prayer for striking out the names of deceased opposite parties on the ground that the case already abated for not substituting the heirs of those deceased opposite parties—the lower appellate court set aside the order of abatement the High Court Division affirmed the appellate order — Held : The High Court Division rightly held that the amendment made by the Calcutta High Court before 1947 is a part of Bangladesh law and are effective as other laws in Bangladesh—the heirs of the deceased defendants were not necessary parties because their predecessors in spite of receipt of notices of the original cases did not appear and file any application for ratable pre-emption as co-petitioners—-petition is dismissed. [Paras- 6 & 7]

Most T. Banu & Ors. Vs. Md. Yusuf Ali & Ors. 4 BLT (AD)-82.

Order-22 Rule-4(4)

In the instant case a definite Saham measuring 1.31 acres of land was allotted to deceased defendant No. 5 Abdus Salam he had and after his death, his legal representatives have a right to get possession in their allotted Saham with reference to the existing possession of the parties but unless they were brought on record their interests can be said to be properly safeguarded by the action of the Advocate Commissioner, against whose report written objection had already been filed. Since evidently the final decree was passed against deceased defendant No. 5 Abdus Salam, after two months of his death without bringing his legal representatives on record by way of substitution, it is to be held that vital interests of the petitioners have been adversely affected in effecting the final decree in their absence. [Para-7]

Kabirunnessa & Ors Vs. Abdul Shahid & Ors 5 BLT (HCD)-189.

Order-22 Rule-9(2)(3)

Principle on Abatement

Abatement on the death of a party to a legal proceeding follows automatically unless his heirs and heiresses are substituted within the prescribed time. To substantiate the legal representatives of the deceased party on setting aside abatement, the applicant is required to prove that he had no earlier knowledge about the death of the deceased party and he had no laches and negligence in making the prayer for setting aside abatement. In view of the fact t.hat abatement Is essentially a technical default, which may deal a shattering blow to his claims, the court is usually inclined to consider an application for setting aside abatement liberally, unless there are gross laches and negligence on the part of the applicant. [Para- 12]

Garakh Nath Shil Thakur Vs. Md. Fatuddin Mondal & Ors. 7 BLT (HCD)-202.

Order-22 Rule-10

In the instant case, Late Protab Chandra Das, in the year 1332 B.S. dedicated the suit properties to his family deities by registered Arpannama. Last Shebayet Chitta Ranjan Das migrated to India in 1981 without making any arrangement to perform Sheba Puja and look after the debattar property. That the local Hindu community in a meeting formed a broad-based trust committee and elected the appellant as its Secretary—the appellant as the Secretary of the Committee is entitled to be substituted in place of Shebayet-defendants. [Para-9]

Faguni Majumder Vs. Mokbul Hossain Biswas & Ors 7 BLT (AD)-12.

Order-22 Rule- 10

Defendant No. 3 as plaintiff filed a suit for declaration of his title to the suit land and obtained an ex parte decree against the present opposite parties—Defendant No. 3 transferred the suit land to the present petitioner by a registered kabala after cx parte decree. The opposite party Nos. 1-5 have filed a title suit for declaration that the ex parte decree is void—the petitioner filed a petition for adding him as party to the suit when the trial was started but the learned trial court rejected the petition— the interest of defendant No. 3 in suit land has been devolved upon the petitioner by a registered kabala, so the defendant No. 3 has got no interest in the suit land and if he does not contest in the suit the petitioner will suffer—hence in the interest of justice, the petitioner should be added as party to contest the suit—Rule made absolute. [Paras-2 & 6]

Rafiqul Alam Bhuiyan Vs. Gazi Alam & Ors 2 BLT (HCD)-137.

Order-23 Rule 1(2)

As to the formal defect or mistake there is no legal bar in granting an application for withdrawal of a suit with liberty to instituted a fresh suit for the same cause of action even at the revisional stage if the other requirements are fully complied with. [Para-7J

Abdul Wahed Mia Vs. Saia Khatun 3 BLT (HCD)-148.

Order-23 Rule-1(2)

The grounds for withdrawal with permission to sue afresh on the same cause of action must necessarily be vital defects which out at the very root of the plaintiffs case and renders him non-suited. It is thus manifest that where the trial court dismissed the suit not only on formal defects but also for want of merit in the plaintiffs case, permission to withdraw the suit with liberty to sue afresh on the same subject matter is clearly not contemplated In law. [Para- 10]

Md. Habibur Rahmaa Paiker Vs. Sree G. G. Datta & Ors 6 BLT (HCD)-146.

Order-23 Rule-1(2)

In this case no permission to sue afresh was either sought or accorded. The plaintiffs’ suit was dismissed and the withdrawal of the suit without any permission to sue afresh will not prejudice any vested interest of the defendants who cannot be vexed with any further litigation on the same cause of action. The defendants will not suffer. The order of setting aside of the decrees of dismissal while according permission to withdraw the suit being in consequence of the order of withdrawal is perfectly justified. [Para-5]

Abdur Rahim & Ors. Vs. Kheru Malitha & Ors. 5 BLT (AD)-216.

Order-23 Rules-1 and 2

Withdrawal of suit and institution of fresh suit for the same subject matter

The plaintiff is at liberty to withdraw his suit at any stage without any permission from the Court but he needs permission for withdrawal if he wants to sue afresh on the same cause of action, without which he shall be procluded from bringing a fresh suit on the same subject-matter. An appeal being a continuation of the suit, it is always open to the appellant to unconditionally withdrew his appeal without the intervention of the Court. According permission to the appellant to withdraw his appeal but refused to allow his prayer to file afresh suit on the same cause of action is illegal and arbitrary. [Para-91

Shaymal Chandra Roy Vs. Probhat C. Roy 7 BLT (HCD)-212.

Order-26 Rule-1

Commissioners power—Trial Court on application of the plaintiff, passed order that the deposition of the plaintiff who is a pardanshin lady would be recorded on commission by an Advocate Commissioner at her residence—the Advocate Commissioner fixed 22.6.89 for taking down the deposition but the plaintiff having with an application on 21.6.89 supported by a medical certificate and prayed for shifting the date. Commissioner rejected her prayer and submitted report to the trial court staling that the plaintiff was not ill.

Held: The Commissioner has exceeded the jurisdiction in two ways, first, the application of the petitioner to adjourn the date for taking down her deposition in not submitting the same to the court for necessary order and secondly, observing that it seemed to him that she was not ill, disbelieved medical certificate. [Paras 1 & 3]

Rabeya Khatum Vs. Asst. Comm. Housing & Settlement & Ors. 3 BLT (HCD)-160.

Order-26 Rule-1

For examination of the widow mother on commission—witness is very much pardanshin and never goes out of her residence after the death of her husband — the application for examination of the widow mother of the petitioner on commission is allowed. [Paras - 2 & 3]

Pallab Kumar Deb Vs. Gonendra Chandra 5 BLT (HCD)-18.

Order-26 Rule-5

Defendant No. 1 is an ailing person and he is suffering from several diseases and is bed-ridden at Karachi but his attorney is living in Bangladesh and is capable of giving evidence and contest the present suit on behalf of this principle. Even his son being young man could come from Karachi and depose the case—the application for examination of the two witnesses at Karachi was rightly rejected. [Para-71

Shawkat Ara Begum Vs Md. Wajuddin & Ors 2 BLT (HCD)-226.

Order-26 Rule- 12(2)

An issue has to be framed on acceptance of the evidence (the report of the Accounts Commissioner) before the suit goes on trial as contended by the petitioners counsel.

Held : According to this provision it is discretion of the Court to direct further inquiry if court thinks fit on examination of the report submitted by the Accounts Commissioner. Acceptance of the report and order to consider at the time of hearing cannot be said that submission of the report simpliciter makes it obligatory on the part of the court to consider the same which according to the provision is evidenced before trial—in this case the Artha Rin Adalat has rightly directed that the report would be considered at the time of pre-emptory hearing of the suit. [Paras-9 &10]

Serajuddin Hawlader Vs. Pubali Bank 4 BLT (HCD)-80.

Order-26 Rules-13 and 14

Commission to make partition of immovable property and the procedures to be followed by the Commissioner

Order 26 Rule 13 of the Code authorises the Court to issue commission to make partition of undivided properties according to the rights declared by the Court while rule 14 provides the procedures for the Commissioner to prepare and allot sahams to the contending parties and to submit report to the Court. After hearing any objection against the Commissioners report, the Court may vary or set aside the report on the merit of the objection.

In the instant case, on receipt of an application for execution of the award decree the learned Execution Court straightway issued writ to the Commissioner for effecting delivery of possession to the applicant in an undivided and unspecified joint property without making the preliminary decree final in accordance with law. The action of the Execution Court is evidently illegal and arbitrary. [Para- 10]

Md. Mizanur Rahman Khan & Anr Vs. Mrs. Jinnatul Ferdous & Ors. 7 BLT (HCD)-278.

Order-32 Rule-3

In Rule 3 the word “shall” is construed to be mandatory and not directory. The above provision manifests that a minor is to be represented by a proper person as his guardian in the civil proceedings through the trial, appeal or revision and in no case he would be unrepresented or to be placed ex parte for the one reason or the other. The appointment of a guardian, therefore, of minor heirs of defendant who died during pendency of suit is absolutely necessary. A minor cannot be considered to be a party to suit unless he is properly represented in a suit by a duly qualified and competent guardian. When a minor has legally become a party to the suit, only then the court would acquire jurisdiction to decide the case. Decree passed against an unrepresented minor defendant being a decree against a person not a party to the suit would be without jurisdiction, null and void. In other words it can be said that a decree passed against a minor defendant not property represented is without jurisdiction and a nullity. [Para-48]

Mohammad Azim & Ors. Vs. Doly Islam & Ors. 7 BLT (HCD)-164.

Order-34 Rule-2(1)

In a suit for sale the preliminary decree is drawn up in the same manner as in a suit for foreclosure—the plaintiff-appellant is entitled to interest ‘pendent lite’ i.e. from the date of the institution of the suit up to the date of the passing of the decree. [Paras-18 & 19]

Sonali Bank Vs. M/S Begg and Beg Jute Incorporated Ltd. & Ors. 6 BLT (AD)-174.

Order-37 Rules-1 & 2

Summary procedure on negotiable instruments and institution of summary suits upon bills of exchange, promissory notes etc.—F.D.R. receipts are not negotiable instruments

While depositing money on a fixed deposit or time deposit by a client, the bank issues to him a deposit receipt, which is usually marked as not negotiable. It can, of course, be transferred to third parties by way of assignment but that by itself does not make an F.D.R. receipt a promissory note as defined in the Negotiable Instruments Act. Consequently, the provisions of Order 37 of the Code have no application to F.D.R. receipts. [Para-7]

Rupali Bank Ltd Vs. Federal Insurance Co. Ltd. 7 BLT (HCD)-244.

Order-38 Rule-5

Plaintiffs application for attachment before judgment does not disclose any particulars in support of the allegation which obviously are vague—which calls for an interference revision is allowed. [Para-6]

Md. Ismail Hossain Vs M/S. Himalaya Ice & Cold Storage Ltd. 2 BLT (HCD)-67.

Order-39

Mandatory injunction — it appears that on consideration of the facts of the case the trial court was satisfied that the plaintiff- respondents succeeded in making out a prima facie case for injunction in respect of the disputed shops and that the locking of the same by the defendant-petitioners was contrary to equity and justice. The High Court Division also noticed that the defendant-petitioners received the notice of the application for injunction and pre-empted the plaintiff-respondents in order to forestall all possible orders of the courts in favour of the plaintiffs. In such a situation this court had already held in Abdul Jalil Munshi and another Vs. Abu Bakar Siddique, 35 DLR (AD) 42 that a mandatory injunction was justified, we have nothing to depart from this view. [Para-4]

Bangladesh Railway & Ors Vs. Abdul Mannan & Ors. 5 BLT (AD)-217.

Order-39 Rule-1

(a) The plaintiffs petitioners instituted a suit for partition and in that suit they filed an application for temporary injunction restraining the defendants opposite parties 1-5 from withdrawing compensation money awarded due to acquisition of some of the suit land and prayed also restraining the land acquisition officer from paying the said compensation money to the said defendants — the said defendants 1-5, objected to the said prayer by filing written objection but did not file any written statements when the matter of temporary Injunction was heard — both the courts below refused to grant temporary injunction to the plaintiffs, on the ground that the plaintiffs could not file any documents or papers in support of their claim of title to the suit properties and also held that the plaintiffs might be adequately compensated in the even of their success in the suit — A prima facie case is not necessarily to be shown by filing documents or papers a prima facie case is spelt out in the plaint in which the partition will go on trial and as such the court has to consider the question whether there is a good prima facie case or not on careful consideration of the pleadings but the courts below have a finding that there was no prima fade case without considering the pleadings — the judgment and orders — of the courts below are set aside the prayer for ad interim injunction as prayed for is allowed. [Paras-2, 6 & 7]

Abdul Jabbar Vs Sultan Mia & Ors 2 BLT (HCD)-139.

Order-39 Rule-1

In the declaration suit the plaintiff prayed for temporary Injunction which was rejected by the trial Judge after holding that as the disputed madrasha had already been shifted but lower Appellate Court granted the prayer for temporary injunction after holding that the defendants could not produce any paper before the court for showing that the said madrasha had already been shifted to the new site. This being purely a finding of fact High Court Division found that the balance of convenience is in favour of the plaintiff and has rightly refused to interfere — hence maintained the injunction order. [Paras - 1 & 3]

Md. Abul Hossain & Ors Vs. Md Salamatullah & Ors 2 BLT (AD)-58.

 

Order-39 Rule-1

The lease having been granted initially for 3 years it cannot be said that the plaintiff has acquired continuing right in the suit fishery after the expiry of the lease period. The learned Judges of the High Court Division rightly considered the reported decision of 40 DLR (AD)-62 and refused to grant injunction as plaintiff has no inchoate right over the fishery which can be protected by an order of injunction. [Para-5]

Mathshyajibi Samabaya Samty Ltd. Vs. The Revenue Deputy Collector & Ors 4 BLT (AD)-228.

Order 39 Rule-1

Mandatory requirements—l find from the original plaint flied along with revisional application that the lands of S. A. Khatian No. 593 Dag Nos. 2338 and 2329 have not been fully described — they are not entitled to get any relief even if they succeed in proving their title—relied on 42 DLR (HCD) 434. [Paras-18 & 19]

Abdul Hashem Mollah & Ors. Vs. Akiluddin & Ors 4 BLT (HCD)-202.

Order-39 Rules-1 & 2

Read with Section-151

Temporary mandatory injunction—in an appellate stage—affairs of the executive committee on one side and the ad-hoc committee on the other side—it appears that the executive committee of the plaintiffs claim themselves as the lawful committee as duly elected committee and their claim is their life, the life of the plaintiffs executive committee has been lawfully and duly extended by the general body of the samity wherein 107 members including defendants No. 2-10 were also present- Held I find that the learned District Judge acted within his inherent power and has rightly allowed the plaintiffs prayer for temporary injunction and restraining the defendant Nos. 1 and 2 from disturbing the plaintiffs in the management of Mymensingh-Dhaka Coach Malik Samity till disposal of the suit. [Para-50]

AminuI Haque Shameem & Ors Vs. A. K. M. Shamsuddin & Ors. 4 BLT (HCD)-154. 

Order-39 Rules- 1&2

Admittedly, State Acquisition Record of Right stands in the name of the plaintiff school. The claim of the defendant Mosque that the record of right standing in the name of the plaintiff school is wrong cannot be determined in this inter-locutory matter like temporary injunction and that can be decided only by legal evidences on the institution of a proper suit to that effect. The plaintiff has filed rent receipts showing payment of rent to the Government and also city corporation or municipal tax receipts evidencing payment of taxes to the city corporation.

This payment of rent to the Government and tax to the city corporation prima facie manifests plaintiffs possession on the suit property and the plaintiff is entitled to get an order of injunction at least to preserve the subject matter In dispute in status quo. [Para- 12]

Lakshmi Bazar Shahi Masjid Committee & Anr Vs. St. Francis Xavier Girls High School 7 BLT (HCD)-237.

Order-39 Rule-1

Whether an order of temporary injunction can be granted by a civil court in respect of a sale notice published under Article 34 of the Bangladesh Shilpa Rin Sangstha Order, 1972 in view of the embargo put under Article 34(5laXiii) of the said order -

Bangladesh Shilpa Rin Sangstha Order, 1972 is a special law and the Sangstha has got the authority to publish the sale notice for the purpose of selling the industrial concern—Held: it is palpably clear that the learned trial Judge as well as the learned Judges of the High Court Division acted illegally and without jurisdiction in granting temporary injunction in a matter covered under Article 34 of the BSRS order which is a special enactment and it will prevail over general law. [Paras - 10 & 11]

Bangladesh Shilpa Rin Sangstha Vs. Aziruddin Choudhury 7 BLT (AD)-81.

Order-39 Rule-1

Whether ad interim status quo order need to be reasonable order

Both the petitioner and respondent No. 5 are claiming the goods. The petitioner is claiming the goods as importer and respondent No. 5 is claiming as auction purchaser of the said goods. Thus we feel that the status quo order need to be maintained till disposal of the writ petition. [Para-5]

M/S. South Asia Mercantiles Vs. Commissioner of Customs & Ors. 7 BLT (AD)-144.

Order-39 Rule-2

Mandatory injunction — in a case where parties are entitled to revoke or dissolve the agreement — High Court Division in effect held that the trial Court ought to have heard the respondents before issuing an ex parte order of ad-interim mandatory injunction, with which we find no reason to differ. [Para-9]

The Dhaka Sangbadpatra Workers Bahumukhi Samabaya Samity Limited Vs. The Dainik Janakantha & Ors 4 BLT (AD)-247.

 

Order-39 Rule-2(3) Read with

Section-151 Order-21 RuIe-32(2)

Suit for declaration that the result published by the Chittagong University is not binding upon the opposite party No. 1 due to the fault that the college authority did not send the tutorial marks to the university — High Court Division found on evidence on record that the authorities did not send the tutorial marks to the university before publication of the examination result of the opposite party 1—Court directed the varsity to add 50% of the tutorial marks to the total marks 322 obtained by the opposite party No. 1 — Rule discharged with modification of the impugned order.

University of Chittagong Vs A. K. M. Monirul Haque & Ors 1 BLT (HCD)-70.

Order-39 Rule-7

Belated—In the facts of the present case it will riot be fit and proper to allow an inspection when the plaintiffs admittedly obtained possession of the unit in 1984 and when, after having unilaterally enjoyed possession thereof for five years, applied for inspection in 1989 when the unit was still in its possession—it will be an idle exercise to allow inspection at this stage. [Para-7]

Shafi A. Chowdhury & Anr. Vs. Bangladesh & Anr. 6 BLT (AD)-164.

Order-39 Rule-7

Appointment of an Advocate Commissioner

—Court had jurisdiction to ascertain the identity of the land which is the subject matter of the application under Order 21 Rules 100 and 101 of the C.P.C.—Held: We find no fault with the order of the High Court Division passed in discretion. [Para-5]

Jebunnessa (Rima) Vs. Mrs. Poneen Abedin & Ors 7 BLT (AD)-341.

Order-40 Rule-1

Simply because the property in suit was under the management of a receiver for a long period of time it cannot be regarded as a just and convenient ground for appointment of a receiver as Order XL Rule (1) does not authorise court to do so on such a ground.

Kamiruddin & Ors Vs M. Mokshed Ali Biswas & Ors. 4 BLT (AD)-4.

Order-40 Rule-(1) (a)

There is no bar in rule-1 of order-40 for the appointment of a receiver during the pendency of the appeal. [Para- 15]

Shamsuddin Ahmed and Ors Vs Bangladesh 1 BLT (HCD)-1.

Order-40 Rule-1

Appointment of receiver

It appears that the trial court with a view to saving the property of the suit from being sold in auction due to non-payment of tax and duties passed the order for appointment of receiver with an observation that whether the plaintiffs have acquired any right, title in the suit property will be decided in the suit itself. Upon such finding of the trial court and in the facts and circumstances Of the case it cannot be said that the learned Judge of the High Court Division has committed an error of law In upholding the impugned order of the trial court. [Para-8]

Mohammad Mosharef Hossain & Ors. Vs. Jalal Uddin Ahmed & Ors 7 BLT (AD)—211.

Order 40 Rule-1(2)

Whether a co-sharer in exclusive possession to be ousted therefrom by a receiver

Held : Suit for partition admitted position being that defendant Nos. 2-4 have been asserting their exclusive control over the income of the petrol pump in question, although they claim that they have been doing the business investing their own capital in the said petrol pump which originally belonged to their father, late Md. Imam Sharif, the common ancestor of both the parties of suit, it does not appear that the learned Judges of the High Court Division have passed the impugned order of appointment of receiver inequitably and in violation of Rule 1(2) of Order 40 C.P.C. [Para-8]

Mohammad Moslem Khan & Ors. Vs. Mohammad Mohsin Khan & Ors 7 BLT (AD)- 101.

Order-41 Rules-11(2) & 19

It appears that the order dated 24.1.94 was passed at the time of admission hearing of the appeal and as such the order was passed under Rule 11(2) of Order of the Code of Civil Procedure and therefore, the application for re-admission of the hearing filed under Rule- 19 of Order-41 of the Code of Civil Procedure is maintainable. [Para 6]

Otaruddin Mollah Vs. Nesaruddin Molla 7 BLT (HCD)-350.

Order-41 Rule-12

Written statement—Opposite parties No. 1 & 2 filed a written statement for the first time in appeal, the Appellate Court accepted the written statement—Held : The written statement is to be filed in the trial court according to the provisions of Order-8 Rule(1) of the Code—the Appellate Court fell in serious error of law in allowing the opposite parties No. I & 2 to file their written statement for the first time in appeal and in accepting the same for the Appellate Court does not have such power. [Paras-8 & 9]

Narayan Chandra Saha & Anr Vs. Jatindra Chandra Saha & Ors 7 BLT (HCD)-303.

Order-41 Rule- 12(1)(2)

After admission of the appeal it is a mandatory to serve notice upon the respondents fixing a date for hearing giving sufficient time to appeal and answer the appeal on such day. [Para- 12]

Abdul Wahab Biswas Vs. Abdul Matin Mia & Ors. 7 BLT (HCD)-227.

Order-41 Rule-21

Ex parte disposal of an appeal on merit is by itself no ground to refuse a relief under Order 41 Rule 21 of the Code of Civil Procedure when the applicant proves his case of prevention by sufficient cause. [Para-12]

Md. Abdul Haque Vs. Md. Mostafa Mondal & Ors. 7 BLT (HCD)—146.

Order-41 Rule-23

The two Courts below concurrently found that the plaintiff failed to discharge the onus to prove that the impugned documents were obtained by fraud. How could an order of remand be made to fill up the lacunae left by the plaintiff himself? The High Court Division also ignored the concurrent finding of the Courts below that the defendants have been in possession of the suit land on the basis of the sale deeds in question. The order of remand was therefore absolutely uncalled for. (Para- 11]

Md. Nazir Hossain Khan & Anr Vs. Shahida Begum & Ors 7 BLT (AD)—7.

Order-41 Rule-23

When a case should be remanded

Suit for Specific Performance of Contract— On a reference to the judgment of the High Court Division it is seen that it held that the real question of controversy has not been adjudicated on the basis of evidence. Upon such finding the High Court Division remanded the case the trial Court for the ends of justice and ordered that the parties should be given opportunity to prove their respective case in accordance with law. As the High Court Division remanded the case for fresh trial with liberty to the parties to adduce evidence to prove their cases the order of remand was made legally we do not find that the impugned judgment and order of the High Court Division occasioned any failure of justice. [Para-5]

Amal Bhushan Singha Vs. Khalakuzzaman & Ors 7 BLT (AD)—311.

Order-41 Rule-23

Remand—We hold that the Division Bench ought to have either dismissed the appeal• for default or ought to have adjourned it to some other date as it was a part-heard appeal or could have passed other orders but it was certainly not authorised to consider the appeal in the absence of the appellant and decide it on merits. It was simply an unacceptable manner of disposal of the appeal and in that view of the matter, the First Appeal ought to be remanded to the High Court Division for fresh hearing on merit. [Para-7]

Govt. of Bangladesh &Anr Vs. Waqer Ahmed & Ors 7 BLT (AD)-367.

Order-41 Rule-23

Remand—when the courts below decided the suit on merit on the basis of the evidence on record, the High Court Division is not at all justified in law in sending back the case on remand to the trial court for holding trial afresh, rather in the interest o1b justice the High Court Division itself ought to have decided the case on merit on the evidence on record and in accordance with law.

Indrojit Kundu & Ors Vs. Sekander Ali 7 BLT (AD)-145.

Order-41 Rule-23

The Family Appellate Court cannot exercise power in sending the suit back on remand to the Family Court for disposal and it can only decide the appeal keeping its authority within the fourwalls of the Family Court Ordinance, 1985 itself. [Para-10]

Md. Ataur Rahman Vs. Ainunnahar 7 BLT (HCD)-241.

Order-41 Rule-23

On remand—In the present suit learned Subordinate Judge has committed a mistake while distributing the saham which has not been done by metes and bounds. It appears that he has distributed the property leaving aside Kha schedule property which was sold by the defendent No.1 to defendant No.2 but that has also must come with the partition and this may be allotted to defendant No.1 which admittedly was inherited by the plaintiff and defendant No. 1—We are inclined to send the case back to the trial court for fresh hearing and disposal of the matter. [Para -16 & 17]

Birta Roy Chowdhury Vs. Amullya Roy Chowdhury & Ors. 7 BLT (HCD)-80.

Order-41 Rule-23

The predecessor of the appellant as plaintiff instituted the Title Suit — the Trial Court decreed. In revision High Court Division found that there are misreading of evidences and that both the Courts below have not at all considered the material evidence on record and for that he send the case back on remand to the trial court — it is not consonance with equity and justice that an old case of 30 years could be remanded so lightly as has been done by the High Court Division even if it is accepted that there is misreading of evidence and non-consideration of material evidence then the High Court Division was within its competence to dispose of the matter on the materials on record without remanding the suit. [Paras-4 & 7]

H. A. Chowdhwy & Ors Vs. M. A. Amin & Ors. 3 BLT (AD)-131.

Order-41 Rule-23 Read with Section- 151

High Court Division observed, it is amply clear that the conduct of the defendant No. 1 has been vexations from the beginning with a motive to delay the proceedings, probably because the property in the city of Dhaka is under her long possession—Held: Even compensatory costs as awarded in the instant case cannot justify an order of remand in the name of ends of justice when the order itself defeats justice. [Para-9]

F Alam & Ors. Vs. Zobaida Nahar & Ors 5 BLT (AD)-88.

Order-41 Rule-23

Order of remand by the appellate court on preliminary point not proper when the said preliminary point was raised in the trial court and judgment was passed on discussion of the entire evidence on record adduced by both parties. [Para-7]

S. M. Shahjahan Vs. Md.  Akmal Hossain 5 BLT (HCD)-19.

Order-41 Rule-23

Remand—whether a particular document is a deed of sale or deed of gift can only be decided on discussion of evidence— the case ought not to have been sent back on remand after 22 years.

‘Where on the basis of the materials on record the appeal could be disposed of by the lower appellate court, It should be disposed of in accordance with law without any fodder forenamed”. [Para-6]

Mst. Saleha Bibi Vs. Taib Ali & Others 1 BLT (HCD)-57.

 

Order-41 Rules-23 & 25

In a second Appeal, in an old case of 27 years of the passing of the impugned judgment—Held : In order to do complete justice and by way of practicing the principle preached above as to avoiding an order of remand, we ourselves looked into the evidence of the 7 P.Ws. and feel satisfied that the evidence of possession is fully uniform coming from competent witnesses and there is no major discrepancy or infirmity in the said evidence—the appeal is allowed. (Paras -13 & 14)

Kabir Ahmed & Ors Vs. Nurul Islam & Ors 6 BLT (AD)-253.

Order-41 Rule-23

Remand—Suit jote originally belong to Mohir Sheikh and Iman Sheikh—the opposite party claimed title to the suit land on the basis of an auction purchase by the opposite party No. 1 for the share of Mohir Sheikh. Share of Iman Sheikh has not been auction- sold and the petitioner purchased the share of Iman Sheikh and from disinterested heirs of Mohir Sheikh—so, since the holding has not been petitioned amongst the co-sharer and both the parties are co-shared of the suit properties and the permanent Injunction suit generally cannot lie in such a holding as the petitioner filed the suit for injunction against co-sharer with a misconceived idea and the court decided the title of the suit property against him—the Courts below decided the partition suit on the basis of the title and possession decided in the suit for permanent injunction between the parties — the partition suit is sent back on remand for fresh trial. [Paras-6 & 7]

Md. Hurmuj Ali Sheikh Vs Amullah Ch. Guha Chowdhury & ors 2 BLT (HCD)-195.

Order-4 1 Rule-28

The suit was filed on 14.9.8 1 praying for a decree for permanent injunction restraining defendant petitioner and others from declaring the Boalia Siddikia Bilateral Madrasha closed and shifting the movable assets of the said Madrasha to some other place—even if the Madrasha was as reported by the Advocate Commissioner closed on 20.11.81 the cause of action for the suit was very much present at the time of the filing at the suit on 14.9.8,1 and when the order for ad interim injunction was passed, plaintiffs opposite parties filed miscellaneous case for violation the order of injunction passed by the learned trial court but the trial court did not dispose of the said miscellaneous case, prior to the disposal of the main suit, further the trial court has dismissed the suit without considering the deposition of the plaintiff and papers filed by him. In view of the above the learned Appellate Court had reasons to set aside the judgment of the trial court. The learned Appellate Court in his elaborate judgment discussed the necessary of taking further evidence for the pronouncement of the judgment and for proper adjudication of the suit—the appellate court may allow evidence or document to be produce or witness to be examined—order for remand should not be made when there Is any specific provision in the Code which would meet the necessity of the case. [Paras- 10 & 14]

M. A. Satter Debipuri & Anr Vs B. Madrasha 3 BLT (HCD)-155

Order-41 Rule-30

It has long been held that under Order 41 Rule 17 CPC the use of the word may” does not mean that it is open to the Appellate Court to dispose of the appeal on merit in the absence of the appellant. [Para-4]

Govt. of Bangladesh &Anr Vs. Waqer Ahmed & Ors 7 BLT (AD)-367.

Order-41 Rules-23,24 & 25 Read with Section- 107

The plaintiff suit being a suit for partition, the question of benami character of the two deeds could be gone into and well decided by the appellate court and a separate relief of declaration of title on the question of benami character of the deeds was not required and even if there was an application for amendment of the plaint in corporation the relief of declaration of title and that application could be disposed of by the appellate court and appellate court was quite competent enough to dispose of the side amendment matter — the lower appellate court was fully competent to decide the case by itself all the evidence and other materials on record were sufficient to enable It to come to a final decision without entailing the parties unnecessary trouble and expenses — there was no necessity for sending the suit back on remand to the trial court. [Paras-20 & 32]

M. K. Bhuiyan & Ors. Vs. Most. Lutfnnaher Begum & Ors. 5 BLT (HCD)-95.

Order-41 Rule-31

The appellate court being the final court of fact must arrive at its own independent findings on the issues involved in the case.[Para-8]

Amirunessa & Ors Vs Abdul Mannan Howlader & Ors 3 BLT (HCD)-245.

Order - 41 Rule - 31

The object of Rule 31 of Order 41 of the Code of Civil Procedure is to see that the appellate Court does not act mechanically in concurring with the findings of the trial Court. It requires that the appellate Court must discuss and consider the material evidence on record and come to its independent conclusions on all points at issue on the basis of the evidence. The appellate Court is also required to set aside the material findings of the trial Court with reference to the evidence on record adverting to the reasons assigned by it. In the case of affirmance general agreement of the appellate Court with the findings of the trial Court may be considered sufficient but in case of reversal the discussion of evidence must necessarily be fairly elaborate. [Para- 14]

Sattendra Nath Roy Vs. Md. Mokshed Ali & Ors. 7 BLT (HCD)- 195.

Order-41 Rule-31

The learned Subordinate Judge did not discuss about the evidence of the witnesses and furthermore he did not controvert the findings of fact arrived at by the trial court. in that view of the matter the judgment and decree passed by the Subordinate Judge are liable to be set aside. (Para-5)

Jobeda Khatoon Vs. Shorab Hossain & Ors. 7 BLT (HCD)-290.

Order-41 Rule-31

Whether the judgment of the High Court Division was not a proper judgment of reversal

It is imaginable that defendant No. 1 by virtue of his very dignified and powerful position in the administration in aid of the Martial Law Authority was in a position to

enlist the support of the Sub-Zonal Martial Law Authority to get his personal end served at the cost of an ordinary citizen of the state. The evidence on record leave no room for doubt that the plaintiff was subjected to coercion, intimidation and undue influence into making the compromise which has been sought to be set aside. The trial court noticed all these facts and more. The appellate court lost sight of’ these salient facts of the case and misdirected itself in reversing the judgment of the trial court without any discussion of evidence and without adverting to the reasoning of the trial court. [Para- 13]

Abul Hossain Vs. Farooq Sobhan & Ors 7 BLT (AD)-389.

Order-41 Rule-31

Non application of judicial mind

On scrutiny of the records we find that the application for setting aside the abatement was made only after 14 days and not 7 months of the order recording abatement as opined by the learned Single Judge. We also find that the application by the respondent under Order 1 Rule 10 of the Code has not yet been disposed of. It is also a fact that the alleged existence of a daughter of Khairunnessa was canvassed for the first time before the High Court Division and that also without any support of evidence. Again, all throughout haziras were filed before the trial court on behalf of the deceased defendant Khairunnessa till 20 July 1985 when Nurul Islam made an application disclosing her death. It is obvious that the plaintiff had no inkling of the death of Khairunnessa till 20 July 1985. It is only in or about the middle of November, 1985 that the plaintiff seems to have the definite knowledge of the death of Khairunnessa without leaving any heir behind. He then came up with an application on 17 November 1985 praying for an1endmnt of the plaint by way of substituting the Government for Khairunnessa, The learned Assistant Judge, however passed an order on 22 December 1985 recording of abatement of the suit.

The plaintiff made the application for setting aside the abatement after the order was passed on 22 December 1985 which is within 14 days of the order. The learned Judge of the High Court Division completely overlooked these facts and set aside the order of the learned Assistant Judge dated 13 August 1987. The learned Single Judge laid unnecessary stress upon certain averments in the written statement which were only matters of contest between the parties at the trial and had no bearing upon the abatement. In our opinion the impugned judgment of the High Court Division is a product of non application of judicial mind and suffers from patent illegality. [Para-7]

Md. Badruzzaman Vs. Begum Shamima Naz Siddique & Ors 7 BLT (AD)-344.

Order-41 Rule-31

Whether impugned judgment is not a proper judgment of reversal

In the instant case the appellate court did not advert the reasonings of the trial court and also did not discuss the material evidences which were considered by the trial court and these hit the root of the merit of the case—and it also appears that the appellate court also did not comply with the requirements of Order 41 Rule 31 of the Code of Civil Procedure in delivering the impugned judgment—Held : The impugned judgment and decree is not a proper judgment of reversal—relied on 1997 BLT (AD) 15. [Para-5]

Md. Harejuddin Mondal Vs. Md. Palu Sarder & Ors. 7 BLT (HCD)-229.

Order -41 Rule-31

The learned lower appellate court by the finding arrogated himself to the position of a legal adviser as such committed an error of law resulting in an error in its deision occasioning failure of justice in as much as advising the parties before him to file partition suit is not the function of a Judge. 1st appellate Court being the final Court of facts misdirected himself both on law and fact and acted illegally in reversing the judgment and decree of the trial court without assigning sufficient and cogent reasons as contended by the petitioners counsel.

Held: On perusal of the judgment and decree of the trial Court I find that learned appellate Court having misdirected himself both on law and facts in course of the judgment impunged travelled for beyond the scope of rule 31 of order 41. [Para - 11]

Md. Kamal Bhuiyan Vs. Anowar Hossain & Ors. 4 BLT (HCD)-60.

Principles of Law laid down on reversing the Judgment and Decree passed by the

Court below

The trial Court decreed the suit holding that the defendant by making unauthorised changes in the structures of the suit premises rendered himself ejectable therefrom. The High Court Division did not at all reverse such finding of fact in reversing the decree of the trial Court. [Para- 11]

Musammat Mohsena Khatun Vs. M/S. Habib Knitting Mills. 5 BLT (AD)-12.

 

Order-47 Rule-1

Though the application was described as under section 151 of the C.P.C. but Court is not to be guided by the description in the heading of the application but by the contents of it as if the petitioners filed an application for review of the order on the ground of mistake and also on the face of the record or by any other sufficient cause the interference of the court would have been perfectly justified even if, the petition instead of being described as for rectification under order 47 rule 1 of the C.P.C. it has been described as under section 151 of the C.P.C. as contended by the learned counsel for the petitioners.

Held: The application filed by the plaintiff petitioners may be treated as an application for review under order 47 rule 1 of the Code of Civil Procedure though wrongly it has been described as an application under section 151 of the Code of Civil Procedure and the merits of the application should be reconsidered and though the appeal in question has been finally disposed of there is a scope for review under order-47 rule 1—the rule is made absolute. IPara-271

Md. Misir Ullah Vs. Syed KhaZiuZlah Malek & Ors. 4BLT (HCD)-38

 

Order-47

In the case of review of a decree under order 47 of the Code the date of the decree will always be the date on which the decree is reviewed, the scope of order 47 is wider than that of sections 152 of the Code. [Para- 101

Bangladesh Vs. Laxmi Bibi & Ors 2 BLT (AD)-182.

 

Order-47 Rule-1

Application for review will be governed by Article 173 of the Limitation Act, the prescribed period for which is 90 days and not by Article 52 of the same, the prescribed period for which is 30 days. [Para-4]

Shawkat Ara Begum Vs. Md. Wajuddin & Ors 2 BLT (HCD)-226

 

Order-47 Rule-1

Review of a part of the order—The order was made upon a wrong assumption that the plaint did not contain any prayer for the said relief. Such an erroneous assumption of material fact amounts to an error apparent on the face of the record calling for a review of the order. [Para-6]

Md. Abdul Jabbar Vs. Bangladesh Bank & Ors 7 BLT (AD)-151

Order-47 Rule-1

The amendment application—It is well recognized that a review can be allowed only on showing that the order or the decision recorded by the court suffers from a flagrant error of law apparent on the face of the record. The review can never be allowed to be utilized as an opportunity for rehearing a matter which is closed by a decision recorded by a Judge. [Para- 16]

Muzaffar Hossain Vs. Md. Shahidullah & Qrs. 7 BLT (HCD)-208.
