Code of Civil Procedure, 1908 (V of 1908)

Section-2(II) Read with Order-20 Rule- 12

The present suit was not an SSC suit but regular Title suit and there is no reason why means profits cannot be allowed. [Para-41]

Parimal Ranjan Das Vs. Mrs. Nasima Khatoon 5 BLT (AD)- 108

 

Section-9 and Order-7 Rule-11

Civil Courts can try all suits which involved the determination of any civil right

— If the circumstances of the case permit, Court can grant such relief as not claimed in the plaint application for rejecting the plaint has got no merit — Rule discharged. [Paras-6 & 8]

Zainal Abedin Vs A. K. M. Fazlul Haque & Ors 2 BLT (HCD)-77

 

Section- 10

Where a party seeks relief under section 10 C.P.C. to stop further proceedings of a subsequently instituted suit between the same parties, it lies squarely upon the applicant to show to the court that a multiplicity of action in the subsequent proceeding is vexatious and totally unwanted. One essential but of the applicability of section 10 C.P.C. is whether the decision in the earlier suit will operate as resjudicata in the subsequent suit. Even if the applicant succeeds in proving that some of the issues of the two suits are common but others are not, still then he is not entitled to get further proceedings of the subsequent suit stayed till the disposal of the previous suit. [Para-6]

Md. Shahabuddin Mian Vs. Agricultural Varsity 6 BLT (HCD)-33.

Section- 10

The proceeding of any special court cannot be stayed on the ground of filing a suit under the general law even that is for the self-same matter and between the same parties. On the contrary suit filed under the general law may be stayed in appropriate circumstances. [Para-20]

Iftekhar Afzal Vs. Pubali Bank Ltd. & Ors. 6BLT (HCD)- 166

Section- 10

Plaintiff instituted Title Suit No. 1S1 of 1994 for a declaration that the plaintiff is the sole owner of schedule property, subsequently the said plaintiff brought a suit being Title Suit No. 131 of 1994 for permanent injunction—defendant petitioners filed an application for stay of the subsequent suit being Title Suit No.- 131 of 1994 till disposal of the earlier Title Suit No. 151 of 1994. Learned Senior Assistant Judge rejected the application of the defendants on the ground that the two suits are not of same nature and character and the cause of action in the two suits are different—Held I find that at least two suit plots in the above two suits are the same and in two courts proceeding are pending and to avoid conflict of judgments and to avoid possibility of multiplicity of proceeding, the subsequent suit should be stayed. [Para – 25]

Shamsul Huq Vs. Ashkor Ali 4 BLT (HCD)-9.

Section-11

Barred by the Principles of Res-judicata—In the present suit the plaintiff has been litigating in respect of the same property against the same set of persons under the same title that the property is an enemy property, raising the identical objection that the agreement for sale was a false, forged and fabricated document as had been raised in the previous suit and as such, in view of the provisions of section 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure the plaintiffs suit is barred by the principle of res-judicata. [Para- 14]

A. D. C. (Rev.) Vs. Most. Anju Bthi & Ors 6 BLT (AD)-51

Section-24

Five suits are pending in three different courts according to their respective valuation since the parties are litigating claiming title to the same property by filing several suits, justice demands that all the suits should be tried analogously by one court. [Para-31

Md. Nur Hossain Vs. Mst. Bibi Halt ma & Ors 5 BLT (HCD)-35

Section-24 Read with Order-47 Rule-1

(a) Section 24—An application for transfer of a case or suit from a Subordinate Judge Court to the High Court Division to any other Court is to be heard by a Division Bench and not by a Single Judge. [Para-4]

Abdur Rashid Khan & Ors Vs. A Hye & Ors 2 BLT (HCD)-211.

(b) Order-47 Rule-I— An application for transfer is to be heard after Issuance of notice when such application is filed before a court. In civil order no such notice was issued which the learned Judge transgress the limits of his jurisdiction In making direction to transfer the case that a direction to dispose of the same within specified period of time. — Section 24 C.P.C. does not refer to a judge but to the Court, application for review is competent. [Paras-2 & 5]

Abdur Rashid Khan & Ors Vs. A. Hye & Ors 2 BLT (HCD)-211.

Section-34

Whether the court can award an interest or compensation in a money suit for the period prior to the institution of the suit for loss of business for non-payment of the balance of the price of goods supplied by the plaintiff to the defendant.

When the court pass a money decree, it may order interest to be paid on the principal sum adjudged from the date of the suit to the date of the decree in addition to any interest adjudged on such principal sum for any period to the institution of the suit with further interest on the aggregate sum so adjudged from the date of the decree to the date of payment. More simplified, the court has power to award interest for three distinct periods (1) the period from the date a sum Is payable to the date of institution of the suit, (2) the period during which the suit remains pending and (3) the period from the date of decree till payment of the Decretal amount. [Para-7]

Sonali Bank Vs. M/S. Karnaphuli Works Ltd 2 BLT (AD)-78.

The Court can allow interest for a presuit period if the principal sum is fixed and payable at a definite time and such conditions are provided for in any agreement between the parties or in any substantive law. [Para-10]

Sonali Bank Vs. M/S. Karnaphuli Works Ltd 2 BLT (AD)-78.

Section-34 (2) (4)

In the instant case the court as well as the appellate court assailant about interest of the amount claimed by the petitioner. So, where the decree doesn’t provide for interest It will be deemed to have been refused provided that which is not done inadvertently or due to mistake. When interest is not awarded on the decree it cannot be executed. [Para-4 ]

Bangladesh House Building Finance Corporation Vs. Most. Amena Khatun & Ors 4 BLT HCD)- 167

 

Section-47

Stay of Execution

Admitted position is that in pursuance to the decree passed in Title Suit No. 68 of 1990 which was a suit for specific performance of contract, the plaintiff got the kabala executed and registered through Court and it appears that possession was also obtained in most of the suit land excepting of course a very small fraction of the land which is in possession of some unauthorised persons. The High Court Division found that since the decree has already been executed in Execution Case No. 18 of 1994 and the kabala has been registered on 20.10.1994 there is nothing to stay all further proceedings of the aforesaid execution case. The petitioner filed Title Suit No. 244 of 1994 for a declaration that the ex parte decree passed in Title Suit No. 68 of 1990 was illegal and void which has nothing to do with the aforesaid execution proceeding and when the decree obtained by respondent No. 1 has already been executed, we are of the view that the

High Court Division has not committed any wrong or illegality in refusing to stay further proceedings of aforesaid Execution Case No. 18 of 1994. [Para-4]

Tapan Kumer Basak Vs. Gouranga Ch. Tarafdar & Ors. 7 BLT (AD)-310.

 

Section-48

The decree-holder obtained the decree on 12-8-59 and the decree-holder’s son filed the latest Execution case more than 18 years after the decree was obtained — Held: The latest Execution Case No. 5 of 1977 filed on 26-8-77 is barred by section 48 of the Code of Civil Procedure and that the High Court Division erred in law in holding that section 48 C.P.C. has no manner of application in this case. [Para – 13]

A. D.C. Pabna Vs. Md. Abdul Halim Mia 4 BLT (AD)-90.

 

Section - 66 (1)

Interpretation of section 66 (1) — When a suit is instituted by the real owner claiming his title against the benamder and the benamder comes forward and resist the claim of the real owner, the matter ends there and the Suit is hit by section 66(1) of the Code. But where the real owner instituted a suit against the benamder claiming that benamder is not the real owner simply benamder and if the benamder or any one claiming under him does not come forward to contest the claim of the plaintiff in that case, section 66(1) of the said Code will have no manner of application and the suit would not be barred under the said Provisions of the Code — in the present case, since the benamder or his heirs did not contest the suit, the suit is not hit by section 66(1) of the Code of Civil Procedure. [Para -14(a)]

Sananda Mohan Barua & Ors. Vs. Niranjan Proshad Barua & Ors 4 BLT (HCD)-187.

 

Section-91(2)

The primary allegation Is in fact one, which affects the plaintiff and this unlawful action of the defendant causes private nuisance to the plaintiff. Sub-section (2) of section 91 of the Code can be invoked in the case of private nuisance. [Para-7]

Wahid Mia Vs. Dr. Rafiqul Islam & Ors 7 BLT (AD)-26

 

Section 96(3) Read with Order-20 RuIe-4(2)

The opposite parties 1-4 as plaintiffs filed the suit for specific performance of contract — the evidence was closed of both the parties the date of arguments, a compromise petition was filed by defendants No. 1 and 2 and the plaintiff No. 1 on behalf of the plaintiffs No. 2-4 — the pleadings of the suit was proved by plaintiff No. 2 for all the plaintiffs as P.W. 1 — In such circumstances no actual authority was given to the plaintiff No. 1 by the plaintiffs No. 2-4 and also to the lawyer to prefer this compromise petition before the trial court — the order passed by the learned Munsif was not proper and accordingly to law on such compromise petition — appellate Court was justified in sending the case on remand for arguments and deliver judgment and pass decree on merit. (Paras-4 &13)

Md. Jamal Abedin Vs. Jugal Ranjan Sukal & Ors. 2 BLT (HCD)-97.

 

Section- 103

Whether the High Court Division was justified in reassessing the evidence as to the date of demand for reconveyance within Magh 1365 B. S. and coming to the findings that the demand was not made within that period and that the suit was barred by limitation?

Held : We have no hesitation to hold that the learned Single Judge of the High Court Division was perfectly justified In exercising his power under section 103 and giving his decision as to the tender of the consideration and demand of reconveyance particularly when, as It appears from the judgment of the High Court Division. the learned Judge was loathe to send back the case on remand to consider this point as was prayed by the learned Counsels, more than 20 years having then elapsed since the institution of the suit. [Para- 12]

Ali Ahmed and Ors Vs. Nazimuddin Patwary 5 BLT (AD)-84.

 

Section-114 and Order-47

Neither non-consideration of material evidence nor prolongation of litigation is a ground for review — non-consideration of material evidence, Ext. 7 (the report of the advocate commissioner) is a ground for appeal not a ground for review. [Para-3]

Mullari Bibi Vs Nurul Islam & others 2 BLT (HCD)-38

 

Section-114, Clauses (a) and (b) Read with Order-47 Rule-1

Review from a decree or order of a Court of Small Causes will be maintainable not under clause (c) but under clauses (a) and (b) of section 114 read with Order 47, Rule-1 CPC. [Para-4]

Gajendra Nath Mondal & Ors. Vs. Motia Begum & Ors. 7 BLT (AD)-280.

 

Section - 115

Revision is impliedly barred because the Artha Rin Adalat Act being a special legislation setting up a special court, the remedies will follow as provided therein. [Para-211

Sultana Jute Mills Ltd. Vs. Agrani Bank & Ors 2 BLT (AD)-127.

 

Section- 115

Period of limitation — Section 115 C.P.C. is an empowering provision granting discretionary jurisdiction to the High Court Division to correct any error of law committed by any subordinate Court resulting in an en-or in the decision occasioning failure of justice. In appropriate cases High Court Division may suo motu exercise such jurisdiction to rectify failure of justice. But as a matter of long standing practice one has to exercise vigilance and promptness in invoking the revisional jurisdiction at the earliest opportunity without causing any inordinate delay. Preferably within 90 days from the decree or order complained against as has been prescribed for preferring an appeal to the High Court Division from any decree or order of a court subordinate to it — relied on 39 DLR (AD) 205. [Paras - 5 & 6]

A.D.C. (Rev) Vs. Md. Abdul Majid & Ors. 4 BLT (AD)- 166.

 

Section- 115

Whether the order passed by the learned Artha Rin Adalat is subject to appeal or amenable to writ jurisdiction or from such order a revision lies under Section 115 of the Code of Civil Procedure?

As Proviso the Section 7 (1) of the Artha Rin Adalat Act, 1990 speaks relating to interim order, the order impugned is amenable to writ jurisdiction as contended by the petitioner’s Counsel.

Held : The Artha Rin Adalat is a civil Court and is subordinate to the High Court Division. That being the legal position we do not find that the petitioner cannot seek relief under section 115 of the Code of Civil Procedure against the impugned order, in as much as, Section 115 uses the expression ‘Where no appeal lies” Section 115 applies. Therefore on this Count we are not inclined to invoke our jurisdiction under Article 102 of our Constitution. [Para - 9]

Serajuddin Hawlader Vs. Pubali Bank 4 BLT (HCD)-8O.

 

Section-15

Whether an order passed by the Artha Rin Adalat (a court of special jurisdiction) is revisable by the High Court u/s 115 C.P.C.

Held: Artha Rin Adalat, though a special court, is nevertheless a court, subordinate to the High Court Division and is, therefore, amenable to the revisional jurisdiction of the High Court Division. [Para – 14]

Sonali Bank Vs. M/S Alt Tannery Ltd & Ors. 4 BLT (HCD)-113.

 

Section-115

The first two courts below concurrently found that the plaintiff had no possession in the suit lands and that without a prayer for recovery of khas possession the suit as framed was not maintainable but the learned Judge of the High Court Division did not reverse the said findings and thus committed an error of law in passing his judgment as contended by the learned counsel for the appellants.

Held : We are of the opinion that the learned Single Judge of the High Court Division acted beyond his jurisdiction under section 115 of the Code of Civil Procedure in setting aside the concurrent findings of facts and sending back the case on remand to the trial Court. [Paras-20 & 21]

Rupe Jahan Begum & Ors. Vs. Lutfor Ali Chowdhury & Ors. 5 BLT (AD)-94

 

Section-115

Whether the High Court Division exceeded its revisional jurisdiction in setting aside the concurrent findings off act

It appears from the impugned judgment that although the learned Judges have stated that the Courts below based their judgments upon misreading and non-consideration of the evidence, yet they failed to lay their hands on any part of the evidence of P.Ws and D.Ws or on any documentary evidence to bring home this error of law on the part of the courts below. Without reversing the findings of the courts below on the grounds mentioned in Section 115 C.P.C the High Court Division has no jurisdiction to disturb the final findings of facts. It cannot superimpose itself as a third court for fresh appreciation of evidence. That is not its function in the revisional jurisdiction. [Para-9]

Md. Shah Alam Vs. Most. Farida Begum 5 BLT (AD)-219.

 

Section-115

The exercise of the revisional power under section 115 of the Civil Procedure Code is a discretionary one. Ordinarily it is not to be exercised where there is an alternative remedy open to a party. [Para-3]

Mrs. Renu Begum & Anr Vs. Kazi Liakat Ali & Ors  6 BLT (AD)-83.

Section-115

Recommending amendment in the Muslim Family Laws Ordinance, 1961 - Prohibiting Polygamy

Suit for prompt dower and maintenance—It was totally unnecessary for the learned Judges to indulge in the discussion on polygamy in Islam which was neither an issue in the suit nor required to be decided in the context of the pleadings of the parties. The exercise undertaken by the learned Judges was not only gratuitous but wholly illegal being not within their jurisdiction under the Code of Civil Procedure

—In the circumstances of the case, we feel compelled to observe that the discussion on polygamy in Islam and recommendation thereon as recorded in the impugned judgment should be taken to be deleted lest it may create confusion in the mind of the Subordinate Courts and the people at large. (Para-51

Md. Elias Vs. Jesmin Sultana 7 BLT (AD)-289.

Section-115

It appears that the trial court on consideration of the oral evidence on record, the content of Ext. C and other documents held that on the refusal to receive the summons of the said suit by said Wazed Au Fakir, the same was served by hanging and in accordance with law in presence of mokabela witnesses namely, D.Ws. 4 and 5, but the lower appellate court without considering the evidence of those mokabela witnesses wrongly held that the summons were not properly served upon defendant No. 1 of that suit. The learned Judge of the High Court Division having, thus, found fault with the appellate courts judgment, in our opinion, rightly set aside the judgment and decree of the lower appellate court in exercise of his revisional authority. [Para-6]

Lokman Fakir & Ors. Vs. Abdul Jabber Bayati & Ors. 7 BLT (AD)-19.

Section- 115

The Trial Judges ordered the return of the plaint to the plaintiffs advocate—Held:

The Trial Court acted without jurisdiction in ordering return of the plaint and therefore the revisional jurisdiction was rightly attracted. [Para- 11]

Shahajazdpur Central Co-operative Bank Ltd. Vs ML Majibur Rahman & Ors 7 BLT (AD)-5.

Section—115

Miscarriage of Justice—Sufficient cause having been found by the trial court the learned Single Judge acted wrongly in exercise of his revisional jurisdiction in interfering with a determination of fact. In revision such an interference has in fact caused miscarriage of justice. [Para-9]

Arosh Ali Vs. Shah Taslimuddin Qurashi & Ors. 7 BLT (AD)-147.

Section -115

Per Mustafa Kamal, J: There was no prayer for amendment of the plaint, not even before the Appellate Division. If in revisional jurisdiction the High Court Division rides roughshod over both substantive and procedural law then a litigant does not know what will happen to his case, what course will it take and what relief will ultimately emerge. This is a travesty of justice, as we know it. The suo motu exercise in the manner it was done, besides being without jurisdiction was an act of extreme judicial indiscretion. (Para-76)

Per Bimalendu Bikash Roy Choudhury, J: Plaintiff No.1 Shamsun Nahar Begum never appealed against the decree of the original court nor did she take any appeal therefrom. She did not also prefer any revision. In such circumstances the learned Judges of the High Court Division had no jurisdiction to give her any further relief beyond what was granted by the first two courts below. (Para- 161)

Mr. Hefzur Rahman Vs. Shamsun Nahar Begum & Ors 7 BLT (AD)-33.

Section- 115

Revisional authority under section 115 of the Code of Civil Procedure will not interfere with the exercise of discretion of the courts below except where the discretion has been shown to have been exercised arbitrarily or capriciously or perversely or where the courts ignored the settled principles of law regulating grant or refusal of interlocutory injunction. Applying the above rule indicating the scope of interference in revision against the exercise of discretion of the courts below to grant the interlocutory injunction. [Para-12]

Lokshmi Bazar Shahi Masjid Committee & Ors Vs. St. Francis Xavier Girls High School 7 BLT (HCD)-237.

Section-115

Maintainability—order of a Family Court—against the order of a Family Court either final or interlocutory and both are appealable under section 17 of the Family Court Ordinance, 1985—instead of presenting an appeal before the learned District Judge, look a revision petition under section 115 of the Code which is not at all maintainable. [Para-9]

Md. Atiqur Rahaman Vs. Ainunnahar 7 BLT (HCD)-241.

 

Section- 115 Read with Constitution of Bangladesh Article- 109

Under the provisions of Article 109 of the Constitution this Court has control and superintendence over all subordinate courts and under the provisions of section 115 of the Code of Civil Procedure this Court can call for the records of any case from any subordinate Civil Court and can pass an appropriate order. If any presiding officer of any such Court fails to comply with any order or direction of this Court made in any case then such officer is not only guilty of contempt of this Court but also of insubordination. [Para-4]

The State Vs. Mr. Faruque Ahmed 7 BLT (HCD)-251.

Section-115(1)

Undisputedly Gopalgonj Pourashava was created in the year 1972. Plaintiff filed the suit in 1968 on the basis of her taking settlement in 1948. Thus when both the trial court as well as the lower appellate court upon consideration of both oral and documentary evidence held that the plaintiff in 1355 B.S. took settlement of the suit land as an agricultural land, the learned Judge of the High Court Division appears to have acted illegally and without jurisdiction in reversing a concluded finding of fact in exercise of his revisional jurisdiction and thereby misdirected himself in holding that the suit land is a non-agricultural land and that the plaintiffs settlement of the suit land having not been made by a registered instrument she did not acquire any valid title thereto. [Para- 12]

Mrs. Nirmala Bala Das Vs. Ganesh Chandra Dhupi 7 BLT (AD)-358.

Section- 115(1)

A Single Judge exercising jurisdiction under Section 115(1) C.P.C. was not invested with the jurisdiction to strike down a piece of legislation which is the absolute and exclusive jurisdiction of a properly constituted court exercising jurisdiction under Article 102 of the Constitution. [Para- 11]

Husna Jahan (Munna) Vs. Md. Shahjahan (Shajal) & Ors. 7 BLT (AD)-98.

Section-115(1)

Whether the High Court Division in exercise of his revisional jurisdiction acted wrongly in setting aside the findings of fact of the lower Appellate Court and has taken a contrary view on reassessment of the evidence

Thus on a careful consideration of the oral and documentary evidences, attendant facts and circumstances of the case, we hold that the lower appellate court in fact did not consider certain material evidence in this case and the surrounding facts and circumstances relevant for consideration of determining the nature of benami transaction and fell into an error of law occasioning a failure of justice calling for interference by the High Court Division in its revisional jurisdiction. [Para-25]

Abdul Karim & Ors. Vs. Muf. Serajuddin Ahmed & Ors 7 BLT (AD)-160.

Section-115(1)

Revisional application is in competent—Interlocutory order in a case for probate or letters of administration before the District Judge—we are of the view that every order including Interlocutory order passed by the District Judge is subject to appeal. [Para- 111

Anuj Chowdhury & Ors Vs. Sallendra Kishore Chowdhury & Ors 7 BLT (HCD)-342.

Section-115(1)

Final Order—when the High Court Division in exercise of its revisional jurisdiction can pass final order in spite of the fact that both the courts below failed to pass any such final order.

Where the evidence on record are enough to pass an appropriate order the High Court in exercise of revisional jurisdiction can decide the case finally and conclusively without remanding It to the lower appellate court. [Para-7]

Mst. Saleha Bibi Vs. Tath Ali & Ors. 1 BLT (HCD)-57.

Section-115 (1)

High Court Division exceeded his jurisdiction in revision in entering into a question of fact and in comparing the signatures himself to arrive at a contrary finding of fact. The finding of fact as to non service of Summons made by the trial court was not perverse, nor was it such as could legitimately justify an interference by the revisional Court on accepted principles. [Para- 10]

Wazed Ali Sardar Vs. ML Afsaruddin Sardar and Ors. 4 BLT (AD)-1.

Section - 115 (1)

Shifting of the school to the new site— the revisional court is competent to interfere in a case of non-consideration of material evidence which is specifically material for the determination of the material issue. Namely, the issue of shifting of the school to the new mouza. (Para – 81]

Md. Abu Bakar Siddique Vs. A. D. C. & Ors. 4 BLT (AD)-233

Section - 115 (1)

Revisional authority—in a Suit for declaration—Non consideration and misreading of material evidence of the P.W. s being a question of law the High Court Division was justified in setting aside the finding of possession against the plaintiff of the lower appellate Court. [Para – 61]

Aldi Uddin Mallick & Ors Vs. Jonah Ali Sheikh 4 BLT (AD)- 254.

Section- 115(1)

The revisional power of the High Court Division is supervisory power which may also be exercised suo motu. The natural corollary would be that the High Court Division is not obliged to hear the parties before pronouncing its verdict when the parties concerned had opportunities to appear but refrained from doing so. [Para-6]

Safaruddin & Ors Vs. Fazlul Huq & Ors 5 BLT (AD)-201.

Section-115(1)

Revisional powers—It is no doubt true that findings of fact, whether concurrent or not, are not ordinarily disturbed by the High Court Division in revision. But where there is a misreading of evidence or non consideration of material evidence affecting the merit of the case, the High Court Division can review the evidence and correct the error in exercise of its revisional powers. [Para-81]

Md. Nurul Islam & Ors. Vs. Nipendra Pathak & Ors. 6 BLT (AD)-163.

Section-115(1)

Application under order 41 rule 19 C.P.C.—learned District Judge dismissed the Misc. Case not only on limitation but also on merit—Held: The learned Judge of the High Court Division in the impugned judgment did not at all touch upon the question of limitation, not to speak of reversing the finding in that regard arrived at by the learned District Judge, on consideration of facts, that the Misc. Case in question was barred by 19 days. Thus the impugned judgment of the High Court Division is patently not a proper judgment of reversal. [Para-6]

Surendra Nath Sarker & Ors. Vs. Md. Sheikh 6 BLT (AD)-169.

Section-115(1)

Trial court’s findings affirmed by the appellate court—concurrent findings of fact disturbed without adverting to them— Reversal of two courts’ Judgment in revision is without any legal foundation. [Paras-13 & 16]

Haji Nurul Alam Vs Al-haj Abdus Sobhan 3 BLT (AD)- 135.

Section-115(1) Read with

State Acquisition and Tenancy Act, 1950, Section—91(1)

Subsisting interest at least to the extent of 12 decimal of land in the case jote.

Defect of parties—the pre-emptors definite case is that after his sales Nitya Gopal Biswas was left with no subsisting interest in the case jote and the pre-emptee led evidence to substantiate the said fact. The learned courts below on considered of the evidence on record concurrently found that Nitya Gopal Biswas had no subsisting interest in the case jote after his sales.

Held : — The findings fact arrived at by the learned courts below on all points at issue appear to be well supported by the evidence on record, both oral and documentary, and these do not suffer from any legal infirmity calling for interference in revision. (Para- 151]

Dhirendra Nath Biswas & Ors Vs. Nikhil Chandra Biswas 6 BLT (HCD)-206.

Section- 132(1)

Court has no power to refuse the right under S. 132—Trial Court is directed to appoint another commissioner to record the deposition of plaintiff at her residence on commission. [Para-5]

Rabeya Khanam Vs. Assistant Commissioner Housing & Settlement & Ors 3 BLT (HCD)-160.

Section-139 Read with

The Evidence Act, 1872 Section-2

Ext. 9, the affidavit sworn before the Presidency Magistrate in India—This exhibit has been filed as a documentary evidence in this case and duly proved. The onus of rebuttal that the affidavit is not validly executed and authenticated is on the defendants and they having not done so it is admissible as a piece of documentary evidence. [Para-24]

Abdul Karim & Ors. Vs. Md. Serajuddin Ahmed & Ors 7 BLT (AD)-160.

Section-148

In a case where a court passes a decree for specific performance of contract the court retains the jurisdiction to extend time under section 148 of the Code of Civil Procedure, even though the decree contains a default clause that in default of the plaintiff to make the requisite payment within the period fixed by the court the suit shall stand dismissed. [Para-51]

Idris Shaikh Vs. Jilamori Bewa & Ors 6 BLT (AD)-123

Section- 149

An opportunity to pay the ad valorem court fee

The plaintiffs filed a suit for a declaration that the decree dated 9.1.84 passed in O.C. Suit No. 271 of 1982 was fraudulent, void, inoperative and not binding upon the plaintiffs. Trial court passed a decree declaring that the impugned decree was not binding upon the plaintiffs as prayed for and further set aside the impugned decree. The learned District Judge and the learned Judge of the High Court Division took the view that the decree could not be set aside because the plaintiffs neither prayed for the same nor paid ad valorem court fee as required for the relief under the Law—Held The declaratory part of the decree passed by the learned Subordinate Judge is restored and the other part, namely, setting aside of the decree will also be restored provided the plaintiffs deposit ad valorem court fee in the Trial Court for the, said relief within 3 (three) months from date. [Para- 12]

Md. Umed Ali & Anr Vs. Mst. Hamida Khatoon & Other 6 BLT AD)-273.

Section – 151

Section 151 simply confirms Courts inherent power and this power cannot be exercised where alternative remedies, such as remedies by way of appeal, revision or review are available. [Para- 11]

Bangladesh Vs. Luxmi Bibi & Ors 2 BLT (AD)-182.

Section — 151

Admiralty Court lacking jurisdiction as there is no cause of action to try the suit—the plaint is returned to the filing advocate without rejecting it u/s 151 C.P.C. [Para-161]

Madina Vegetable & Oil Refinery Industries Vs. M.T DOLORES 2 BLT (HCD)-69. 

The provision of the Code of Civil Procedure was not made applicable to the Admiralty Court in the matter of rejecting the plaint hence the order u/s 151 C.P.C. [Para- 161]

Madina Vegetable & Oil Refinery Industries Vs. M.T DOLORES 2 BLT (HCD)-69.

Section- 151

Inherent power of the court— Respondent No. 3 Bank as plaintiff instituted money suit against respondents No. 1 and 2. Suit was decreed ex parte on 27.7.72. The said decree was put into execution In Money Execution Case and filed an application under Order 21 Rule 30 of the Cr.P.C. before the executing court. Executing Court allowed the said application and public auction was accordingly held on 5.11.88— respondents No 1 and 2 filed an application under section 151 of the Cr.P.C. for cancellation of the auction sale and the execution of the auction sale arid the execution court on 27.1.90 was pleased to allow the said application—the executing court has exercised a discretion after the sale become absolute and the learned Judges of the High Court Division on a wrong reliance on the case reported in 41 DLR (AD) 109 upheld the exercise of the discretion—the learned Judges did not act legally in affirming the order of the executing court. Para- 121

Fariduddin Chowdhury Vs. M/S Sylhet Glass Works Ltd. & Ors. 3 BLT (AD)-168./

Section- 151

In the instant case the defendant has disconnected the gas line on 16.3.92 long before the institution of the suit. The plaintiff has not challenged the order or the act of disconnection of the gas line. The gas line is not in continued connection as such the learned Judge acted without jurisdiction injunction on a subject matter not within the suit property. The Court cannot travel the suit beyond the suit property. [Para-6]

Chairman B.O.G.M.C Vs. Abdul Kashem 3 BLT (HCD)-189. 

Section- 151

The inherent power is the last reserve in the hands of the court and cannot be used to remand the case unless there is some violence to the sense of justice which cannot be remedied otherwise than by an order of remand — In the instant case all the evidences and materials were before the lower appellate court and the lower appellate court itself could have disposed of the appeal finally — this is not a case where the court could exercise inherent power under section 151 of the Code in remanding the suit to the trial court for fresh decision. [Paras-23 & 24]

M. K. Bhuiyan & Ors. Vs. Most. Lutfunnaher Begum & Ors. 5 BLT (HCD)-95

Section-151

The inherent power of the court can be resorted to in the interest of justice only when there is no specific provision in the Code of Civil Procedure to meet a particular situation and that too for preventing an abuse of the process of the court or an apparent injustice. [Para-81]

Harendra Nath Mandal Vs. Chitta Ranjan Halder & Ors 6 BLT (HCD)-88.

Section- 151

Law is settled that a proceeding under section 151 of the Code of Civil Procedure cannot be resorted to where there is alternative remedy available for seeking redress. The inherent power conferred under section 151 of the Code can be available in a case where there is no other provision for providing a redress. Power under section 151 of the Code can be invoked by a court only when the court is satisfied that prevention of the abuse of the process of the court is necessary or when ends of justice demand that the wrong complained of would be remedied. In the name of ends of justice, the remedy provided in the Code itself cannot be allowed to be negative and also to be thwarted. The court, of course, under section 151 of the Code preserves the power to set aside order passed under misapprehension of facts when true facts are brought to light. The court also got the inherent power to vacate any order obtained by misleading the court and practicing fraud upon it. The court, in the exercise of the power under section 151 of the Code, also, can correct the unintentional or inadvertent mistake committed by it. The court also preserves the Inherent power to vacate any order if the same is passed under misapprehension of law. But the power cannot be invoked in cases which would result in overriding the express provision of law. [Para- 12]

Amirunnessa & Ors. Vs. Abdul Mannan & Ors. 6 BLT (HCD)-161.

Section- 151

The plaintiff petitioner instituted Title Suit No. 92 of 1987 (was renumbered as Title Suit No. 53 of 1989) for recovery of possession of the suit properties. In the ex parte disposal of the suit the learned Assistant Judge dismissed the same on 7.2.90. But in Civil Revision 962 of 1990, preferred by the petitioner, a Single Bench of the High Court Division on 7.2.9 1 decreed the suit. The petitioner, however, instituted Execution Case No.1 of 1992—Respondent Nos. 1 and 2 as representatives of the deity on 15.11.80 instituted Title Suit No. 1085 of 1980 (was renumbered as Title Suit No. 225 of 1986) for declaration of her title to the suit land. The present petitioner is a party in the case of Title Suit No. 225 of 1986 and that the petitioner in his suit did not implead the plaintiff of Title Suit No. 225 of 1986 as party—Held The High Court Division in the facts and circumstances of the case has rightly refused to interfere with the discretion exercised by the executing court under section 151 of the Code of Civil Procedure in the interest of justice staying further proceeding of the execution case pending disposal of Title Suit No. 225 of 1986. [Para-7]

M. A. Salek Vs. Sree Sree Kripamaya Kali Mata & Ors 7 BLT (AD)-29.

Section- 151

Whether the judgment-debtor-respondents could seek the remedy by filing an application under Section 151 of the Code of Civil Procedure wherein he challenged the execution proceeding itself as illegal and without jurisdiction and prayed for restoration of possession as an ancillary relief after setting aside the entire execution proceeding -

It is to be stated at the outset that the decree of the trial court as passed In Title Suit No. 4 of 1994 was modified by the High Court of the then East Pakistan on 22.3.60. The decree of the trial court having been modified by the High Court it merged into the decree of the High Court. Hence, the question of drawing up of a modified decree on 9.8.93 in the light of the judgment and decree of the High Court in First Appeal is wholly illegal and without jurisdiction. It is found that the modified decree was passed on 22.3.1960 and to avoid the question of limitation a modified decree was again drawn up by the trial court on 9.8.93 and which is so obvious that it was obtained from a court by fraudulent means. Even if, it is admitted that a mistake was committed by the executing court Itself even then there are innumerable authorities of this court to hold that any error or wrong committed by the court itself can be corrected in exercise of its jurisdiction under Section 151 of the Code of Civil Procedure to secure the ends of justice and to prevent the abuse of process of court. Thus, the execution proceeding is apparently barred under Article 182 of the Limitation Act. The plaintiff did not take any steps within three years from the modified decree of the High Court nor he kept alive the decree by taking steps to execute the decree within 12 years from the date of the final modified decree.

Thus in order to avoid the bar of limitation the plaintiff fraudulently got the modified decree drawn up by the trial court. Hence the application under Section 151 of the Code of Civil Procedure is maintainable in the facts of the present case.

Further, the plaintiff got decree for 8 Anna’s share of the suit property as modified by the High Court. In the execution proceeding the application was filed by the decree- holder for partition and for possession. Without filing a partition suit the executing court cannot also pass an order for possession when the decree itself does not contemplate such possession by partition of the property by metes and bounds. This exercise of jurisdiction by the executing court is palpably erroneous and without jurisdiction. [Paras- 10 & 11]

M. Majid Vs. Iqbal Bahar Chowdhury & Ors 7 BLT (AD)-139.

Section- 151

If the plaintiff petitioners are aggrieved in any way due to their own mistakes, they may seek remedy in an appropriate forum, if so advised, but they are not certainly entitled to get a remedy under Section 151 of the Code of Civil Procedure to rectl1r substantive mistakes affecting the merit of the decision. Section 151 of the Code of Civil Procedure is no doubt a special preserve of the Court for doing even-handed justice under given circumstances but the Court is not competent to exercise its inherent power in any and every matter which is not sanction by law. [Para-4J

Harun-Or-Rashid & Ors. Vs. Quyum Khan & Ors 7 BLT (HCD)-34.

Section- 151

Inherent power of the Court to do justice

It is well-settled that no party to a proceeding should suffer due to the act of the Court, one of the first and highest duties of the Court being to take care that its act does not cause any injury to any of the suiters. It will be quite harsh and inequitable if the illegal action of the Commissioner on the basis of a writ issued to him in violation of the provision of law is allowed to stand, driving the aggrieved party to have recourse to other ardorous, costly and time-consuming exercise for getting back possession in the suit property from which it has been dispossessed illegally. In such a case, exercise of the inherent power of the Court under Section 151 C.P.C. is clearly permissible. [Para-12]

Md. Mimnur Rahmart Khan & Anr Vs. Mrs. Jinnatul Ferdous & Ors. 7 BLT (HCD)-278.

Section – 152

Whether the limitation for filing an appeal against a decree will run from the date of the decree or from the date on which the decree has been amended on an application under section 152 of the C.P.C. Answer—from the date of the decree.

Subordinate Judge as an Arbitrator passed the award on 28th May, 1985. The Arbitrator corrected the Award on 10th March, 1990 on an application under section 152 of the C.P.C. The scope of this section is very limited and decision under this section cannot materially affect the decree except correcting some insignificant errors or accidental omission having nothing to do with the merit of the decree itself. The appeal, not being filed within the prescribed period of 60 days from the date of the decree on 28.5.85 but being filed about 4- years beyond this period, was not maintainable. The decree award being under a special law, condonation under Section 5 of the Limitation Act also did not apply. The amendment does not give a fresh start of limitation to file an appeal from the date of the amendment; the point remains as before the date of the decree. [Paras-4, 6 & 7]

Bangladesh Vs Luxmi & Ors 2 BLT (AD)-182.

Section- 152

Advocate — right of address and showing the name for respondent No. 1 — without filing any Vokalatnama the learned Advocate has got no locus standi to file an application for amendment of the judgment and deck ee showing the name for respondent No. 1. [Para – 3]

Arzowara Khatun Vs. Asstt. Custodian Dhaka 4 BLT (HCD)-162.

Section-152 Read with Order-22 Rule-3(1)

Upon plain reading of the provision of sub-rule (1) of Rule 3 of Order XXII, it appears that it is the right of the heirs of the deceased plaintiff to file in court an application for substitution and a corresponding duty has been cost upon the court to make them parties in the legal proceeding, when the right to sue survives. In exercise of their right the appellants well within the period of limitation submitted the required application for substitution furnishing all the required particulars and the same having been allowed by the court they also prosecuted both the Misc. Case as well as the suit after its restoration. From the date of acceptance of the appellant’s said application there was no legal existence of the deceased plaintiff in the case record, whose name could not have been retained by the trial court in the plaint when the suit was restored to its file and number. Clearly an error on the face of the record had been committed by the trial court for not recording the present appellants as substituted plaintiffs in the plaint and for failing to draw up the decree In question accordingly. Under Section 152 C.P.C. the trial court ought to have corrected its own clerical errors even after the passing of the decree. [Para- 11]

Md. Siddique Rahman & Ors. Vs. Profulla Bala Devi & Ors 6 BLT (AD)-57.

Order-1 Rule-9

Suit for Partition - No suit can fail by reason merely of non-joinder of parties. (Para-6)

Safaruddin & Ors. Vs. Faziul Huq & Ors 5 BLT (AD)-129.

Order-1 Rule-10

Sub-tenant is not a necessary party to be added in the suit between the landlord and the tenant — he can be a proper party — has joinder as proper party in the suit cannot alter the nature of the suit. [Para- 10]

Babar Ali Pramanik & Ors. Vs. Meser Ali Pramanik & Ors 1 BLT (AD)-29.

Order-1 Rule-1O

Petitioner claims to be a sebait of the Debottar property of the suit on question on the basis of a power of attorney and wants to be added as party in the suit for protecting that property—the petitioner has failed to produce any document to show his interest in respect of the suit property other than the power of attorney which does not contain any schedule of any property—the petitioner is neither a necessary party nor a proper party and that his presence is not necessary for a effective decision of the suit—Rule is discharged. [Paras-8 & 11]

Hrishikesh Chkrabarti Vs. Sree Sree Mahaprovu 3 BLT (BCD)-131.

Order-1 Rule-10

Whether the petitioners are entitled to be added as parties to safeguard their interest

Plaintiff-respondent No. 1 filed a suit against the defendant-respondents for a declaration that three sale deeds dated 5.5.76 by which defendants No 1 & 2 purchased the suit land are void ab-initio and by virtue of those deeds ‘no right and title have accrued to them. Trial Court decreed the suit on appeal, the Appellate Court dismissed the suit. The plaintiff-respondent then obtained a Rule in Civil Revision which is pending for final hearing — The petitioners are subsequent purchasers during the pendency of the suit, filed an application for addition of parties in the Revision case before the High Court Division — Held: The issue in the suit was whether the three kabala deeds dated 5.5.76 were void ab-initio or not. The issue is not whether the petitioners subsequent purchase of the suit land from the defendants during the pendency of the suit is valid or not. The petitioners are not competent persons to make any submission with regard to the three sale deeds dated 5.5.76—Their applications has been rightly rejected by the High Court Division. [Paras-7 & 8]

Nesmohammad & Ors. Vs. Mst. Jamila Khatoon & Ors. 6 BLT (AD)-276.

Order-1 Rule-10

The petitioner as plaintiff instituted a suit for specific performance of contract and the suit was decreed on contest by judgment and the decree was duly drawn up. After drawing of the final decree the present opposite party No. 1 filed an application for adding him as a defendant in the said suit—opposite party No. 1 had no right to be added as a defendant in the suit which has already been finally disposed of by a regular judgment. [Para-6]

Sushil Chandra Das Vs. Mronjan Paul & Ors 6 BLT (HCD)-174.

Order-1 Rule-10

From the petition under Order 1 Rule 10 of the Code of Civil Procedure dated 2.5.87, marked Annexure “A” to the petition, it appears that the petitioners claimed the suit property as heirs and heiresses of the original tenants Poyer Mamud Mondal and his sister Powchhari Bibi. The case of the plaintiff opposite party is that he got the suit property from his father Poyer Mamud Mondal and fufu Powchhari Bibi by way of settlement on obtaining dakhilas in the year of 1345 B.B.. which facts are stoutly denied by the present petitioners. It has been contended in the application under Order 1 Rule 10 of the Code of Civil Procedure that the original tenants Poyer Mamud Mondal and Powchhari Bibi never settled the suit land with the plaintiff and the plaintiffs claim of title by way of settlement is false. It has further been asserted that as co-owners of the suit property by inheritance like the plaintiff the petitions have been owning and possessing the suit property in ejmali. It was also contended in no uncertain terms that the plaintiffs’ papers in respect of the alleged settlement are totally false and fabricated. It thus appears that vital interests of the petitioners are involvement in the suit and they have definite say in the adjudication of the suit and they are interested in the result of the suit for declaration of title in the suit land. in the face of the clear and specific assertions made by the petitioners it is evident that vital interests of the petitioner are involved in the suit and as such their presence in the suit is necessary for proper adjudication of the controversies between the contending parties. The order of the learned Munsif, rejecting the petitioners’ prayer under Order 1 Rule 10 of the Code of Civil Procedure is thus found to be illegal and arbitrary occasioning failure of justice and as such is same is liable to be set aside in the interest of justice. [Para-9]

Mst. Halima Khatoon & Ors. Vs. Nurul Huda Mondal & Anr 6 BLT (HCD)-1.

Order-1 Rule-10

To be added as proper parties in the writ petition

Added as parties—Held : In view of the fact that the learned Judges of the High Court Division have correctly observed that the writ petitioner having made specific allegations against them, namely that upon their influence, the Ministry of Law has cancelled his appointment those accused-respondents are at least proper parties in the writ petition to refute such allegations. [Para-41]

Md. Borhanuddin Advocate Vs. Mintstry of Law & Ors. 7 BLT (AD)-230.

Order-1 Rule-10

Whether a stranger to the contract, to be added as a proper party

Held: It is true that ordinarily in a suit for Specific Performance of Contract only the contracting parties are the necessary parties. But in view of the peculiar facts that after about 25 years the plaintiff has sought for Specific Performance of Contract dated 15.4.70 in respect of an apparently joint property without making one of its admitted co-sharers namely, respondent No.1, as a party to the suit, the learned Judge of the High Court Division upon proper consideration of the material facts has rightly held that the case of respondent No.1 clearly come within the exception of the general principle of addition of party in a suit for Specific Performance of Contract and that he is a proper party to be added as a defendant in the suit for proper adjudication of the real dispute as to whether the bainapatra in question is a fake one and as to whether there was any family settlement as alleged in the plaint by the plaintiff on the basis of which the contract in question with defendant Nos. 1-3 was entered into. [Para-6]

Md. Toffazzal Hossain Vs. Sunil Kumar Basak & Ors 7 BLT (AD)- 103.

Order-1 Rule-10

Being added as parties in the case for obtaining probate of a Will—Sons of testator were necessary parties in the miscellaneous case for probate. There is no doubt about it. Thereafter, the appellants who claimed interest through the sons of the testator obviously were necessary parties in the probate proceeding. [Para-5]

Abdul Hye & Ors Vs. Khetra Mohon Bawali 7 BLT (HCD)-345.

Order-1 Rule-10(2)

Court’s Power to add or strike out parties Order 1 Rule 10 of the Code of Civil Procedure empowers the Court to add any person to a suit or to strike out the names of any person improperly impleaded therein at any stage of the proceeding if the Court considers the presence of such a party necessary or unnecessary, as the case may be, for the effective adjudication of the proceedings before it. Since the petitioners were not at the scene when the suit was filed but they became Interested in the result of the suit subsequently, they cannot be made co-plaintiff, over the head of the unwilling plaintiffs. But they should be made defendants in the suit to have their full say in the matter for protecting their interest. [Para-7]

Md. Zahirul Haque Chowdhury & Anr Vs. Sanker Lal Deb & Ors. 7 BLT (HCD)-1.

Order-1 Rule-10(2)

Petitioners are to be added as defendants in the suit admittedly the petitioners are in actual possession of a portion of the suit land by way of lease wherein they have constructed a small hut and have been running small shop therein and they are very much interested in the result of the suit and their interests cannot be properly safe guarded by the lessor as contended by the petitioners counsel—Held: Learned Sr. Assistant Judge without proper application of his judicial mind to the facts and circumstances of the case and proper appreciation of the scope of Order-I Rule- 10(2) of the Code of Civil Procedure wrongly and arbitrarily rejected the prayer of the petitioners for impleading their as dependants —the prayer for addition of parties be allowed. [Para -6]

Gobinda Chandra Karmoker Vs. Shanti Ranjan Talukder 4 BLT (HCD)-73.

Order-1 Rule-lO (2) Read with Order-6 RuIe-17 and

State Acquisition and Tenancy Act, 1950 Section-96 (2)

Amendment of the pleadings by way of addition of a party at a belated stage — A

belated prayer for addition of necessary parties or for amendment of pleadings by itself is no ground to refuse such a prayer if such addition or amendment of pleadings be found necessary for complete and effectual adjudication of the matters in issue— relied on 33 DLR (AD) 113. [Para-8]

Mst. Hasina Khatoon & Anr. Vs. Md. Shamsur Rahman & Anr. 5 BLT (HCD)-22.

Order-3 Rule-4 (1)

(1)—The Court found that the power of attorney is forged and fabricated—The Court shall debar the Advocate to act for the party in the court, for the simple reason that he has not been appointed for the purpose by or under a valid power of attorney and has therefore no authority to act on behalf of the party in the Court. The disability attaches to the Advocate and not to the plaint, in such circumstances the trial court ought to have direct for further correct and better power of attorney—May be it was forged and fabricated but that cannot be a ground for disposal of the case. [Paras-8 & 9]

Mathura Mohan Pandit Vs Most. Hazera Khatun 2 BLT (HCD)-215.

Order-3 Rules-1 and 2

A person not a party to the suit nor a husband nor wife nor an attorney got no authority to give testimony in a suit in support of the case either of the plaintiff or the defendant. [Para-86]

Mohammad Azim & Ors. Vs. Doly Islam & Ors. 7 BLT (HCD)-164.

Order-5 Rule- 14

Personal appearance — No party to be ordered to appear in person residing over 200 miles from the court. [Para- 10]

M.S. Progati Industries Ltd. Vs. Md. Abdul Majid Mondal & Ors 5 BLT HCD)-151.

Order-5 Rule- 14

The summons of the original pre-emption case was served on the husband of the pre-emptee-respondent—The High Court Division rightly held that—in the instant case there is no evidence that the husband of the preemptee-respondent was the recognised agent of hers. Therefore the summons was not duly served upon the pre-emptee-respondent. [Para-6]

Abdur Rahman Vs. Shamsun Nahar Begum & Ors. 7 BLT (AD)-125.

Order-5 Rule-17

It appears that on the refusal to receive the summons, the same was served by hanging and accordance with law in presence of mokabela witnesses namely, DWs 4 and 5. In that view of the matter the petitioner’s plea that summons was not served upon them is not tenable at all. [Para-6]

Lokman Fakir & Ors. Vs. Abdul Jabber Bayati & Ors. 7 BLT (AD)-19.

Order-VI Rule-17

Whether in making the prayer for partition by amendment, would change the nature and character of the suit.

(a) The principle is that the nature and character of a suit do not change so long as the fundamental character of the suit remains the same. A suit for declaration of title recovery of possession and/or for partition is essentially based on a common claim of the plaintiff which may call for aforesaid different relief or reliefs in different situations — by adding a relief for partition in a suit for declaration of title and possession there was no alteration to the foundation of the suit and as such the fundamental character of the suit remained the same, there being thus no question of changing the nature and character of the suit appeal allowed. [Paras- 12 & 19]

Abdul Motaleb Vs Md. Ershad Ali & Ors 2 BLT (AD)- 164. 

(b) While allowing or rejecting an amendment of a pleading and for that matter while exercising any discretion under the law, the Court must give its reasons so that when the order is called in question the higher Court may be in a position to see that there has been application of mind by the Court concerned and it was aware of the principles involved in the exercise of its discretion. [Para-20]

Abdul Motaleb Vs Md. Ershad Ali & Ors 2 BLT (AD)- 164. 

Order-VI Rule-17

The evidence on the side of the plaintiffs having been closed and all the plaintiffs witnesses having been examined and cross- examined, a completely new story was attempted to be added in the additional written statement—the learned Single Judge of course observed in his judgment that there is inordinate delay in filing this application for amendment of the written statement but he allowed this by holding that the same can be compensated by giving money and consequently awarded cost of Tk. 1000/- as compensation to the plaintiffs—the principle guiding the amendment of the written statement as contemplated under the law has not been taken note of and the learned Single Judge allowed these revision cases taking a sympathetic view in the matter which is not permitted by law — that the orders passed by the learned Single Judge need be set aside. [Paras-9 & 10]

Abtul Kalam Azad & Ors Vs Sunwar Ali & Ors 2BLT (AD)-4

Order-VI Rule-17

Amendment of the plaint—in the instant case the radical changes were sought to be introduced in the plaint by the amendment sought for and allowed by the court. On the other hand the learned Assistant Judge has not discussed the merit of the application or of the nature and character of the amendment sought for but has passed a summary order allowed the amendment of the plaint. This is no way is a judicial order. The Court didn’t apply its judicial mind in passing the impugned order—Case is allowed. [Para-4]

Samela Begum Vs Chandulltia Midha & Anr 3BLT (HCD)- 130.

Order-VI Rule-17

(a) The guiding principle for amendment is that it ought to be made for the purpose of determining the real question in controversy between the parties to any proceeding or for correcting any defect or error in any proceeding. There lies inherent power of the court and the principle applicable to the amendment of the plaint is also applicable to the amendment of the written statement. [Para-81]

Md. Nazrul Islam Majumder Vs Tahmina Akhter 2 BLT (HCD)- 131.

(b) The amendment of the plaint in family court case — the amendment was sought for by the wife in her own suit the certain fact had happened after the institution of the suit and it is necessary to be taken into notice of the court by way of an amendment for doing complete justice and to settle the real controversy between the parties — The Family Court allowed the said amendment and the learned District Judge affirmed the same — the courts below had rightly done so. [Para- 10]

Md. Nazrul Islam Mujumder Vs Tahmina Akhter 2 BLT (HCD)-131.

Order-VI Rule-17

Amendment of the plaint — During pendency of the civil revision the petitioner filed a petition for amendment of the plaint of the partition suit praying for declaration of title of the petitioner to the suit land — the petitioner prayed for partition of the share of his predecessor in interest and since the opposite party has no claim over this portion of land. The opposite party will not suffer any injury if the amendment is allowed for proper adjudication of the suit — amendment be allowed. [Paras-6 & 7]

Md. Hurmuj Ali Sheikh Vs Amullah Ch. Guha Chowdhury & Ors 2 BLT (HCD)-195.

Order-VI Rule-17

From the reading of the assertions made in the original written statement and in the proposed amendment it appears that the defendant No 3 wanted to change the entire stand taken by her in the earlier written statement. At this the plaintiff will be prejudiced. The application for amendment was rightly rejected by the Subordinate Judge. [Para- 10]

Shawkat Ara Begum Vs. Md. Wajuddin & Ors 2 BLT (HCD)-226.

Order-VI Rule-17

The plaintiff opposite party instituted title suit against the defendant. Petitioners for declaration of plaintiffs title in eight katha of land and for recovery of khas possession of petitioners No. 1 and 2 and another—During the cross-examination the plaintiff opposite party filed an application for amendment of the plaint — In the plaint it has been clearly stated that a boundary wall existed between the land of the plaintiff and the defendant petitioners. The plaintiff should have made a prayer in .the plaint for demolition of the existing boundary wall between the plaintiffs and the petitioner’s land. It appears that plaintiff omitted to make a prayer for the same. As such the plaintiff j.1iould not be allowed to make a prayer by way of amendment at this stage as contended by the learned petitioners Counsel—Held : In the application for amendment there was a prayer made for demolishing of the wall and the super structure raised thereon. In the absence of any statement in the plaint that the defendant petitioner disposed the plaintiff opposite party from the suit land and in absence of any prayer for demolishing the existing wall in the plaint we are of the view that the amendment proposed could at last change the character of the plaint which is not permissible under the law — the order passed by the learned Subordinate Judge is set aside. [Paras- 4 & 5]

Md. Mohiuddin Ahmed Vs. Md. Habibur Rahman & Ors 4 BLT (HCD)-34.

Order-VI Rule-17

From the impugned order it appears that the learned Assistant Judge did not at all applied its mind to the question involved and without disclosing any reason whatsoever rejected the application for amendment — impugned order is liable to be set aside — relied on 13 DLR - 317, 15 BLD - 519, PLD 1970 (SC)-173. [Para-10]

Abdur Rahman Vs. Md. Shamsuddin & Ors. 4 BLT (AD)-173.

Order-VI Rule-17

In the appellate Court plaintiffs No. 1-7 and the appellants filed a solenama on the basis of which the suit was ordered to be decreed and it was remitted to the trial court for the said purpose. The plaintiffs could not be permitted to open the new issue (by amendment) for decision in the suit after having already entered into compromise admitting the claim of the appellants. [Para-7]

Sunil Chandra Mondal & Ors. Vs. Narayan Chandra Shil & Ors. 5 BLT (AD)-10.

Order-VI Rule-17

Whether in the absence of an initial prayer in the plaint for recovery of possession the subsequent prayer would entail a change in the nature and character of the suit, particularly when the alleged dispossession took place after the filing of the suit

The plaintiff instituted the suit for declaration of its title to and confirmation of possession in the suit land. Thereafter the plaintiff filed an application seeking amendment of the plaint by way of adding a prayer for recovery of khas possession in the suit land stating, inter alia that during the pendency of the sine defendant No. 1 in collusion with some of the tenants of the plaintiff dispossessed them from the suit land—Held The plaintiffs application for amendment of the plaint is allowed. [Para-12]

Central Co-operative Bank Vs. Mafijur Rahman & Ors 7 BLT (AD)-5.

Order-VI Rule-17

Suit for Partition—The amended prayer was plaintiffs be allowed a decree to purchase the share of defendant No.8 and consequential relief be passed in pursuance thereof.

The High Court Division held that the plaintiffs can pray for such relief at the initial stage by including the relief in the plaint itself or at any stage subsequent thereto. The only entitlement of defendant No.8 is to file an additional written statement and also to get a reasonable cost from the plaintiffs for filing an additional written statement. We do not think that the High Court Division committed any error of law in holding the said view. [Paras- 4 & 5]

Sharif Abdul Mannan Vs. Mst. Motahara Banu & Ors 7 BLT (AD)-126.

Order-VI Rule-17

It is true that the learned Judge of the High Court Division has not mentioned in the impugned order that in view of the amendment of the plaint the defendant may file an additional written statement if he is so advised. Even in the absence of any such direction for filing additional written statement, the defendant, before disposal of the suit, shall always have the right to submit additional written statement on the amendment of the plaint. [Para-6]

Khondker Monjur Morshed Vs. Khandker Monjur Hasan 7 BLT (AD)-21.

Constitution of Bangladesh, 1972

But they are not applicable in the instant case in as much as Regulation 12 of Bank (Staff) Regulation, like to parent law, being a protected legislation, the provision for termination by notice is not void though it may be inconsistent with any fundamental right. Bangladesh Bank & Ors. Vs. Mohammad Abdul Mannan 2 BLT (AD)-1O1

 

Articles-27, 28, 38 & 44

A violation of fundamental rights in impounding the posters for demanding separate electorate as contended by the petitioner’s Advocate.

Held : No direction to the government can be given for alleged violation of fundamental rights. [Para-3]

Mr Gobinda Chandra Parcunanik Vs. Bangladesh & Ors 3 BLT (HCD)-1O1

 

Articles-27 and 31

Whether the provision of Section 10A of the Public Demands Recovery Act, 1913 offends Articles 27 and 31 of the Constitution

As a policy decision of the Government for early recovery of the loan of Bangladesh Krishi Bank by amendment the provision has been made in the order itself for recovery of Bank dues under Public Demands Recovery Act and for speedy recovery some sections of the Public Demands Recovery Act shall not apply and Section 1OA has been inserted in the Act itself as a special provision for recovery of certain dues as Public Demand—

Held: Thus Section 1OA of the Act which provides for a special procedure relating to recovery of dues cannot be said to be arbitrary and illegal—on a reference to other provisions of the Public Demands Recovery Act, we find that all the defaulting borrowers of Krishi Bank are entitled to equal protection of law provided by the Act by way of appeal, review and revision as contained in Sections 51, 52 and 54 of the said Act and as such the learned Judges wrongly held that Section 1OA offends Articles 27 and 31 of the Constitution. [Paras-8 & 9]

Bangladesh Krishi Bank Vs. Meghna Enterprises & Another 7 BLT (AD)-84

Articles-27 & 31

Whether Section 6(2) of the Artha Rin Adalat Act, 1990 is ultra-vires of the Constitution as it offends Articles 27 and 31 of the Constitution-

The persons who are taking loan from the bank are a class apart and they are all treated equally under the law In force. We do not find that Section 6(2) of the Act Is in any way violative of Articles 27 & 31 of the Constitution. [Para-5]

Chuni Lal Bashak Vs. United Commercial Bank Ltd. & Ors. 7 BLT (AD)-157

Article-27 and Artlcle-29 (1)

If the Government nominates some persons for employment in the service of the Republic in pursuance of a statutory provision or rules the nominated persons acquire a legal right for enforcement of the same. But if the executive prepares a list of persons for appointment in the service of the Republic without the backing of any law behind it and actually appoints some persons from the list, the others left out can come to the High Court Division not for enforcement of any legal right but for enforcement of their fundamental right. Article 27 of the Constitution provides that all citizens are equal before law and are entitled to equal protection of law and Article 29 (1) of the Constitution provides that there shall be equality of opportunity for all citizens in respect of employment or office In the service of the Republic. If the petitioners merely prepared a list and kept it to themselves or their different departments for implementation as and when possible the writ petitioners had nothing to complain about: but when a number of them are appointed from a list and the appointment of others is postponed pending inquiry into the genuineness of a list comprising of 1745 persons with which list the writ petitioners have no concern, then they can legitimately complain of inequality before law and discrimination in public employment—We are of the opinion that the High Court Division was not well-grounded in law in directing the petitioners to absorb/appoint the writ petitioners against specific posts within a specified period which is purely an executive act. We are not inclined to interfere with the same except with the modification that the petitioners will appoint! absorb the left-out writ petitioners as and when vacancies are available. [Paras-6 & 7]

Govt. of Bangladesh & Ors Jahangir Hossain & Ors 7 BLT (AD)—347

Articles-27, 31 & 42

RAJUK invited applications from the interested parties for bid in the auction for Residential Plots for 99 years. In response to that the petitioner filed an application in the prescribe form and he was the highest bidder and he was given impression that in due course he will be given the allotment letter. But RAJUK did not issue any allotment letter in accordance with the terms of the auction but instead they have by notice inviting fresh applications for auction of the said plot for which the petitioner had successfully made highest bid—

Held: We are of the view simply because the petitioner was the highest bidder and when no allotment letter or any notice was served on him to deposit money, he cannot claim any legal right and canvas for any legitimate impression created in his mind for acquiring something which is also a disputed of question of fact, as such the instant writ petition is in competent. [Para- 11]

Dr. Md. HabtbuUah Vs. Rajdhani Urtriayan Kartripakha & Ors. 7 BLT (HCD)-8

Article-28

All the writ petitioners were cabin crews working as absorbed employees of the Bangladesh Biman Corporation, their designation being Flight Stewardess— they shall retire from service on the completion of 57 years of age —The Bangladesh Biman Corporation amended Bangladesh Biman Corporation Employees (Service) Regulation, 1979, substituting regulation 11 and providing therein that a Flight Steward (male) shall retire at the age of 45 years and a Flight Stewardess shall retire at the age of 35 years — the writ petitioners variously challenged amended Regulation 11 — the High Court Division held, the impugned amendment is violative of Article 28 of the Constitution as it discriminates between a male and female member of the cabin crew in respect of their age of retirement — Held : We find no ground for interference. [Paras -3 & 9]

Bangladesh Biman Vs. Mrs. DaRn Perveen & Ors. 4 BLT(AD) -110

Article-31

The order Memo No. 320(19)- Swa:Ma:(Ni-l) dated 10.6.1975 issued by the Ministry of Home Affairs having imposed restriction of the right of the Marwan Community to transfer or other wise to dispose of their property to another and also on the right of the citizen of Bangladesh to acquire property is discriminatory and also violative of the fundamental right guaranteed under the Constitution and the equality clause provided under Article-31—the restriction said to have been imposed to the Marwari Community not by any law but by an administrative order having not the force of law—the Memo No. 320 (19)-Swa:Ma:(Ni-1) dated 10.6.1975 issued by the Ministry of Home Affairs have been made without lawful authority and is of no legal effect. Paras-7 &8

RaJkumer Behani Vs Bangladesh 2 BLT(HCD)-169

 

Artlcle-35 (4)

Orders under Section 4(1) of the Anti- Corruption Act, 1957 — The petitioner of each of the four writ petitions was asked to submit the statement in the prescribed form giving statements with full particulars of the properties acquired in his name or in the benami, the liabilities and the sources of income. On the face of the impugned orders, there is nothing to suggest that the respective petitioner was made accused and formal accusation had been made against him and it cannot, also, be said that as accused person he is being compelled to give evidence against himself. Article 35(4) of the Constitution will be attracted only, if the proceedings ‘started with the accusation’ and the person who seeks its protection is already an accused person and he is of being compelled to make the statement. By the respective impugned order, the respective petitioner has been asked to submit statements with full particulars stating the acquisition of properties and the sources of income so that he can satisiy the Government that the properties acquired by him are not disproportionate to his known sources of income. Calling of statements detailing full particulars cannot be characterised as accusation as contemplated under Article 35(4) of the Constitution.

M. Habibur Rahman & Ors Vs. Govt. of Bangladesh & Ors. 7BLT (HCD)-327

 

Article-38

The refusal of registration of the Trade Union activities in the Bangladesh Rural Electrification Board is violative Of Article 38 of the Constitution as contended by the petitioner’s learned Counsel.

By law the Rural Electrification Board having been exempted from the category of shops or commercial establishment the formation of association, but not of trade union, is permissible, but there is no right of recognition. Further trade union activities in any statutory body setup by an ordinance may be reasonably restricted by and under a law to keep It outside of the ambit of industrial relations ordinance as such the same is not violative of Article 38 of the Constitution. [Para-5]

Abu Hossain & Ors. Vs. Registrar of Trade Union & Ors. 6 BLT (AD)-284

Article - 39 (2)

Majority view - A. T. M. Afzat, C.J. delivering the majority judgment (Mustafa Kamal, J and Mohammad Abdur Rouf J concurring with him).

Interpretation of the Article of the Constitution of Bangladesh—the writ-petitioner-respondents are engaged in the business of publication, distribution and selling of books including ‘note-books’ for primary and secondary schools up to class VIII. The respondents challenging the NoteBooks (Prohibition) Act, 1980 (Act No. XII of 1980). They submitted that the restriction exposed upon publication and sale of the ‘note-books’ In question is violative of the fundamental rights guaranteed by the Constitution—Held: In the facts of the present case, however, we have come to the conclusion that the right to freedom of speech and expression as claimed by the writ-petitioners does not cover or extend to the right of printing and publishing of ‘notebooks’ on ‘text-books’ prepared and published by the Text-Book Board under statutory authority. We, therefore, hold that the High Court Division was not justified in declaring the impugned Act to be unconstitutional being ultra-vires of Article 39(2) of the Constitution. [Para – 30]

Bangladesh National Curriculum & Ors Vs. A. M. Shamsuddin & Ors. 4 BLT (AD)-205

 

Article-40

The Rural Electrification Board took a decision barring all ex-employees of the said Board from participating in any tender to be floated by it. The secretary of the Board communicated the said decision under his office order dated January 30, 1986—the order of the Board is violative of Article 40 of the Constitution. [Para-2]

Chairman, Rural Electrification Board & Anr Vs. Abdul Jalil & Anr 5 BLT (AD)-264

Article-96 Read with Article 99 and

The Public Servants Retirement Act, 1974, Section-5

Appointment was cancelled offering one month’s pay—if such a Judges Service dependent upon the sweet will of the Appointing Authority the Principle of Judicial independence will be a mockery and public confidence in his decisions will be shaken the Public Servants Retirement Act under which the petitioners contract was made does not apply to a retired Judge of the Supreme Court. The appointment, removal and other terms and conditions of service of a retired Judge in a public office should not be governed either by ‘master- and-servant law’ or by any unequal contract. If it is not thought to be expedient to make any statutory provision in the case of such appointment, it is better that the original Article, 99 be restored putting total ban to appointment of a retired Judge to any public office whatever—subject to the observations, the petition is dismissed. [Para-5]

Justice Abdul Bari Sarker vs. Bangladesh 2 BLT (AD)-64

 

Article- 102

Section- 141 of the Code of Civil Procedure does not interns apply to proceedings in writ in the High Court Division under Article- 102 of the Constitution. But the court in its desertion can apply the principles as distinguished from the technical provisions of the Code of Civil Procedure to meet the exigencies of the situation in appropriate cases on the ground of justice equity and good conscience in what situations the principles of the Code of Civil Procedure will be applied and in what extent may perhaps be left to the wise discretion of the court itself. [Para- 15J

Moni Begum & Ors.Vs RAJUK & Ors. 2 BLT(AD)-71

 

Article- 102

Executive committee of the Matsajibi Samabaya Samity being dissolved under section 18(3) and a 5-member Ad-hoc committee being appointed under section 18 (4) of the Co-operative Societies Ordinance, 1984, the writ petitioner appellant preferred an appeal,  although no appeal lay against such order before the District Registrar, who rejected the same by an order dated 23.10.93 against which the appellant moved the writ petition before the High Court Division which was also summarily rejected on the ground that the appellant did not preferred art appeal before the District Judge within 60 days.

It is procedurally absurd to ask the appellant to go to a higher appellate forum to obtain a verdict on the jurisdictional error of the first appellate authority the High Court Division failed to exercise its jurisdiction under Article 102 of the Constitution is not disposing of the appellants writ petition on merit and in requiring him to prefer a further appeal to the District Judge when the first appeal itself was incompetent in the eye of law. [Para- 10]
